O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O thou, dearest son, I have completed this book which is the last of medical knowledge together with its fulfillment; and have brought it to an end by its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And there came unto me in vision that I should complete it for thee with this treatise which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is neglected in our region and has been entirely destroyed throughout, therefore its science has perished and been cut off; and there remains nothing but small descriptions about it in books which hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this ignorance and vanity have come, and intentions are closed and the science has been forgotten.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	Now it seems to me that I wish to enliven it together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	And I will bring together the shapes of the iron tools for cauterization, and other instruments of this work with the arrangement of their declaration and preparation as necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has been neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who engages in this must rise up in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he may know the judgment of the members and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and sinews and the number of joints, and the movement and the moving and resting veins, and the place of their exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And therefore Hippocrates said that a name with a name is much, but with a deed it is little.
et meismement en l’art de main.	And especially in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things said before should beware lest he fall into error and kill men.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	Thus, I have seen many times those who meddle with this science and yet lack both knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish surgeon who cut the abscess of scrofula on a woman’s neck, and he cut the arteries of her neck
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	So that so much blood flowed out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And see also another physician who drew a stone from a man's bladder, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	and he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to him to remove it, and saw the condition of the sick man and the greatness of the stone; and knew well that if it were cut into he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And see also another physician who took in charge the Duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the breaking there was a wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the physician, full of ignorance, tied the fracture upon the wound with strong bandages, and did not leave any lint to the wound, and thus left him.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	And he commanded that it should not be untied;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and so remained until the leg was entirely swollen and the foot came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come unbind the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I had unbound it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all paths were already corrupted in the limb, and it could not be healed;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	And corruption did not cease to travel through the limb until the whole limb was lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another surgeon who burst open an inflamed carbuncle and then burned it through his own wickedness.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a carbuncle, when it is free from melancholic humor, ought not to be touched with iron unless it is in such a place that all that is corrupted can be entirely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And therefore, dear son, you must know that manual labor is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	 namely, work where there is danger in many circumstances;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore, you must be careful so that foolish doctors cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	Take up your arms with caution, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, using the best method so that through God's grace you may come to safety and be praised;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave fearful diseases to those of great skill;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Remove your arms from that which causes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may pass from this world to the next with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galien says in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not undertake serious illnesses lest you be called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	This treatise has been devised according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapter is about fire cauteries and medicinal ointments, from the head down to the feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and about the shapes of instruments, and iron implements for cauterizing, and everything necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, bloodletting cups, wounds, arrow extraction, and similar procedures.
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and the chapter is organized with the shapes of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and twisted injuries, and similar conditions;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	It is organized from the head down to the feet, along with the shapes of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we remember the work, it is necessary for me to tell you about the quality of the temperament and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of a helper and the harm caused by them are lengthy discourse and subtle knowledge, including secret responses
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and about this most wise men spoke at length, and agreed upon it.
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	They spared few words with me, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery helps universally in all complexions where there is matter, whether they are hot or cold.
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	It means that it is to be known as: hot complexion without matter, and dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry complexion with matter together, some said that cautery there is great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery is of no use in diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to treat hot diseases with heat or dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and he who says the opposite claims that cautery greatly helps hot and dry diseases found in men's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the temperament of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it many times through experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in any case, do not meddle with it except those who have tried it and know through long experience the chapter on cauteries, and the diversity of human complexions, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the seasons and the spacing of time.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	Of other constitutions we have no fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians assembled and agreed upon the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Know, my son, that fire alone is the secret of remedies and has greater efficacy than a cauterizing medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple and acts only upon the member which it burns, and does not harm other members if one takes care.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	The burning medicines spread from member to member, causing severe diseases;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	And sometimes they kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire alone and its goodness do not harm unless there is excessiveness.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found by experience and through the length of service and study that I have put into the art, which was based on the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	Therefore I excuse the length of my speech, as it is not my wish to conceal from you the secret that lies in fire and the quality of its work, how it overcomes bodily diseases, as philosophers demonstrate;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	So receive this in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, my son, that they agreed upon the time when cauteries should be performed and chose priests.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	I say that cauterization is suitable at all times, because the harm underneath is removed with the help of cautery;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And especially if cauterization is necessary for sharp and sudden pains that cannot wait until a greater harm comes to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think, dear son, as foolish physicians do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for a disease healed by cautery has no recurrence;
et il le dient ensi;	They say thus:
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	But it is not so as they think, because cauteries are not medicine that changes the complexion and dries up the humors that cause pain; their value lies more in their speed of action than in their power and virtue.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible for disease to come sometimes according to the patient's complexion, where the disease occurs and its strength;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and excesses are gathered in him through the acquisition of foods and similar things; except for cauteries administered where there is little excess or moisture, such as dental cauteries for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return;
mais ce avient poc.	But this happens little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the surgeons of medicine, and that is true;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	But they do not believe that cauteries are worth using after medicine, but their intentions are mistaken, and cauteries are the rear of medicine because when we administer ways of treatments in any disease and they do not work, then we apply cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it is clear that cauteries are the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cauteries made of gold are gentler than those made of iron, and they said this only because of the quality of gold and its high value.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	And they said that the place cauterized does not cause corruption, but this is not true, for I have tried it and found that in some people it is indeed so.
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	And cauteries of gold are worth more than those made of iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And yet when you heat a tool made of gold, you cannot know for sure how hot it is just by its color, and it cools quickly;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	And if it is heated too much;
si font au feu;	If they put it in the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	Thus, there are enough obstacles.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	Therefore, we use cauteries of iron that have been more appropriately prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have arranged this chapter from head to toe so that it is easier to find the way.
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is useful for moistness and coldness on the head. There are two types of it made due to the cause of an illness called "soda," and also because of many humors that flow down from the head to the ears and throat, causing numerous dreams, toothache, sore throat, and especially all illnesses that come from coldness like paralysis, sciatica, apoplexy, and similar ailments.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The shape of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged by a softening solvent medicine for three or four nights, according to what the strength and age and habit of the patient can tolerate;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	And then make him sneeze.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, placing his hands on your shoulders;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	then place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And where your middle finger comes to, then press and heat the cautery called 'olivare', of which this is the shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	Place it on the marked spot, and move downwards and outwards, turning your hand bit by bit;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then lift your hand gently, and reward yourself if you see a little of bone II emerging;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	And if you do not see [the bone], then recommence the cautery until you see it as I have told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	Then take some boiling water, and put soft cotton inside, and place on the location [of the wound], and let it stay for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	Then place soft cloth soaked in butter on top.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	And leave it on until the inflammation is gone.
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound with the ointment called 'tetrafarmacon', until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And as the ancients say, the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges itself;
et por ce si aide mues.	And for this reason, nature aids wounds.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	Some also say that one should leave the cautery on until part of the bone is burnt, and then scrape off what has been burned from the bone and heal it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And others say that the cautery should be left on until it burns away bone as wide as a skein of wool used by women for spinning, so that the humors can exit more freely.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must leave the wound open for an extended period.
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	After the wound, one must dress and heal it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two types of cauteries seem not to be entirely good except in certain men where there is a matter of fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	And it seems to me that I should leave them alone;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	For the head is weakened by prolonged solutions of nature, as we witness in other limbs;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And even when the head of the patient is weak by nature, the first appearance of a cautery seems to me more harmful and dangerous; but I now use this one in common practice with safety.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	For chronic headache
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When the head suffers from chronic pain that lasts a long time, the patient should use ointments and pills called "cochies," and perform purgations of the head using oils and plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	And even if one applies the cautery we mentioned earlier, it will not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Beware that if the head of the patient is strong by nature and not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Then cauterize with this cautery a little below what we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	Afterwards make cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery at the place called 'vessels'.
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	And this is where cupping glasses are placed;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and lift your hand so that you do not see down to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	The patient feels much greater pain from this cautery than from others, and I will speak of it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	And the cauteries on the horns must be more subtle than those used to cauterize the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	"Of the cautery of the head,"
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When sudden pain comes in one part of the head, and the illness extends to the eye, and the head is purged with medicines that dissolve impurities, and all the other treatments I have mentioned in the section on illnesses are performed, but none of them help:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then he applies cauteries in two ways: that is, of medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cautery of medicine is such that you take an aloe stalk, remove the skin and chop it into two pieces, then place them on both temples where the pain resides in such a way that you can place the aloe stalk beneath the skin;
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it has been placed there, let it stay and hold it tightly for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	then remove it and wipe the aloe stalk with garlic, leaving the wound alone for two or three days.
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then place cotton soaked in butter on it until it sticks out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment with ointment until it is healthy;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see that, then apply some burning medications that I have written about in the twelfth chapter on burning medications.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery follows this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery with which is the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closed" because its head is shaped like a keyhole with a slight curvature at the tip, and in the middle there is a small opening;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	And place it on the painful spot, keep your hand there and slightly twist the iron a little, until half of the edge of the heart-shaped knife is burnt.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	Then lift your hand so that the artery does not burn; this is necessary, and there should be an abundance of blood flowing.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Afterwards, place cotton wool soaked in sulfur on the spot for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then place cotton moistened with butter, and then treat the wound with ointment until it heals.
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	And if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called 'cultellare', do so at its tip, but be careful not to touch the artery in this young migraine.
de emigraine	de migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a migraine as we have said before in the division of illnesses, and it does not improve, and you see that the previously mentioned cauteries of medicine and iron do not help, then you must heat the cautery called 'cultellare' until it is white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	And hold steadfastly on the spot a line half as long as two fingers, and lift your hand once, ensuring that you do not compress the artery, and do not go up to the bone.
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	And guard against the mandible that moves when one chews, and ensure the nerve has no regard for the movement, and spasms do not come upon the patient, and guard against the loss of blood from the artery once it is compressed, or compression causes great fear, especially to those unskilled and inexperienced.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	And leave the work in mid-course;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	But I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it is relevant in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that these cauteries are not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is suffering, then cauterize around the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	And if you see it, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And this cautery is better and more helpful than the one without.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	Chapter 49: On the Pain of the Ears Due to Coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When cold pain comes to the ear and one has opened medicinal solutions there and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division, but the pain does not cease, then heat this cautery called "point":
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	Then prick all around the painful ear, or both ears if pain is felt on both sides, and mark the spot a little away from the root of the ear where you will begin;
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	And make ten pricks around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the area until it is clean.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the Torture of the Mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	The torture that must be cured by cautery is only that which moves with the pulse flow, as we have mentioned in our discussion of diseases;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not perform cauteries on those that come from heat and dryness of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you treat this type of torture that moves with the pulse flow and has been cleansed by hydrides and purgations of the head and gargling, but it is ineffective, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	The one at the root of the ear, and the other a little behind the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	Place the cautery on the healthy appearing part, and perform cautery near the top of the ear slightly below the horn of the head, and another at the temple as long as a pea.
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	And leave the cautery until half of the coal is burned.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	This is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it has a similar shape to the scalpel we have placed before, but it is slightly more refined, and the blade should be slightly thicker.
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treating the spot as I said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is advanced and you treat it as we have said, but it does not improve, and the patient has no fever, then perform four cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one where it is called "vessels" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach.
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	And let him be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	de la litargie
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness, it is necessary to give the patient large ointments and pills made from mignonette for the head;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	Then wrap the patient's head entirely, and place on the back of his head the plaster of mustard that is described in the treatise on plasters;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	And this is the manner of the cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	Thus do as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is healed thus, that is good.
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	And if he is not healed, perform three cauteries on the sides of his head down to the neck, with two fingers' breadth between each cautery.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	And treat him as before, and if you see that he does not improve, perform one cautery in the middle of his forehead;
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if necessary, two more on the two temples, and treat until he is healed.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	And let the cautery called "olivary" be used, as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	Pour traire la froideur du chef, il covient mettre li malaides en un lit bien chauffez et bien couverts, et doner lui un bains d’herbes chaudes, c’est à dire verveine et sauge et chouli ou chous vert; aprés doner lui yeres de graisse doree sur le chief, puis li met sus la teste ung emplaustre de canelle et de girofle en poudre mis en un lit dou pain; puis li fai .iij. cauteres emmi le chief comme j’ai dit devant.
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of years and of those things we have mentioned before;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	After this, raise the patient's head, then make a cautery mark on the top of the head and on each horn, and two marks behind and three on the nape of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	And if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is enduring, and the disease is severe, then make four cautery marks on the nape of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and let it burn until the most of the heart is cauterized, then raise your hand.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	After the treatment, once it is healed, use the cautery that is called "olivare" which we have mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not apply cauteries except for the phlegmatic type. First, cleanse the brain of hairs and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and capable of taking medication.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot endure this, perform gargling and chewing to cleanse the brain often with good foods;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	Then raise the child's head in mid-air, and make one cautery mark according to what we have said before, one on the vessel, and one on each horn;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if the patient is strong and enduring, perform cauteries as I have said on those who have paralysis and weakness of body, on the spine of the back and neck, using an olive oil cautery according to the method that I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, apply one subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When the cause of melancholy is the presence of superfluities or corrupt humors and thick phlegm, then apply cauteries as we have said for those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if the cause of melancholy is that superfluities tend towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him to drink something by which the brain may be cleansed, according to what is said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After binding the head of the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	Then make a bandage of well-made linen, like a circle, and place it around the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	And the patient sits crossed-legged, and is held firmly on all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	Then present the linen, melted with old sheep's butter;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	Heat it gently over fire until the dough can bear being placed upon it;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	Then remove the circle from inside the head, and let it cool;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And do this to the patient once each week with another good treatment until they are healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you wish to cauterize a wound by making several pricks all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This method of cautery moistens the brain greatly;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	And then place cotton soaked in butter and goose fat on top.
de l’awe des eulz	For the treatment of eye pain
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When pain first comes to the eyes due to the signs that I have mentioned in the division, begin by giving the patient something to drink that cleanses the head and guards against all moistures. Make him sweat or take baths several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	Afterwards, instruct him to raise his head and make a cautery mark on the head. If both temples are affected by eye inflammation together or if only one temple is affected, apply two cauteries on the two temples or one cautery on the one affected temple.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and cauterize all the veins and arteries that are below the heart, ensuring that the cautery mark is as long as it is wide.
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	And beware of excessive bleeding; if too much blood flows out, stop it with the power you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you about extracting arteries and how to incise and cauterize them.
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And sometimes, one makes a cautery or incision below the two rear bones.
dou cors des larmes	of the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are old and habitual and are on the veins or near the arteries that appear on the forehead from outside;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and it is seen that they are caused by cold humors, then perform the cautery mark I mentioned earlier for treating eye inflammation.
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	For cautery on the head, apply two cauteries above both temples, and two cauteries behind below both cheekbones.
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	And if more is needed, cauterize bloodily above the eyebrow at each small cautery
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	When the aqueous humor descends inside the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you treat according to what we have said in the section on division, and it does not help at all, then give the patient three nights of pigeon broth to drink
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	After that, shave the head and apply a cautery in the middle of the olive-shaped cautery
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	And apply two cauteries called 'clavilis' above both eyebrows, slightly below the eyes
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	Be careful not to touch the artery
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery which is called "olivary".
de coi ci est li forme:	with which is the form
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see fit, apply two cauteries above both eyebrows as long as the eyebrows themselves
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And do not leave your hand there until a third of the paper is burned, according to the manner I have described
dou poil qui point l’oil	Regarding the hair that points at the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes turn inward and prick the eye, in which case cauteries are applied in two ways:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	This is to know of fire, or of burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	Once they have grown and are even, then place the patient in your hands;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	After placing a figure on the paper like the shape of a mirror on the mint, and let it be the beginning of the sign near the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then put moistened cotton on the eye with gum Arabic and powdered peppermint, then heat the cautery of which this is the shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After cauterizing on the figure that you have marked several times gently, so that the skin is burned there;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	And the sign of health in this work is when you see the paper withdraw, and the hairs stand upright at the point of the eye;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	Then lift your hand, and leave it thus for three days, then place cotton moistened in butter until the burning sensation is relieved.
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the ointment treatment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if afterwards hairs come and the paper becomes soft then recommence the cautery on that same spot, just as you did first;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if the hairs are missing, then cauterize until the paper is lifted to its natural place, and is even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The medical fire cauteries are that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make from parchment the shape of the laurel leaf;
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take some French soap and live coals, each one-third part, and grind them well together;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and do it quickly so that it does not cool, then pour it onto the shape you have made like the laurel leaf, and place paper over the eyes;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	And if the patient holds it with one eye only, then operate on one, and if both also.
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	And place moistened cotton under the eye like a wick.
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	And place the patient's head in your lap with both hands over the medicine, and press the pouch until all of the medicine has been applied every time the patient feels biting pain, for they feel as if it were fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	After you have done this for some time, then remove the medicine from your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the biting pain has passed, then raise the lever up and observe if the paper lifts as if it were raised by force of fire or by incision.
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	So if it is so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, apply more medicine to the lever where the medicine did not act, until your work is even and your eyes are fixed.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place moistened cotton in butter until the heartburn has settled, afterwards treat the wound with ointment called 'diaphoresis' and others until it is clean.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary for you to take great care with your work, so that no error occurs in administering medicine to the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick in the eye, then recommence the cautery on that spot softened by the paper itself, even as you have done before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment until it is healed;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And this is the form of the mold for the mirror:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	Know that human eyes vary in size and smallness, and adjust your constraints accordingly.
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And let not the straight path be blocked for him who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Regarding the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you are treating a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then it is necessary that you perform a cautery on it in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put their head in your hand;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	And the master should hold their head between his hands in such a way that it does not move nor bend its head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	Then put moistened cotton on egg white or in colchicum juice onto the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	Then heat the cautery that is thus shaped:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	And is raised at its end like the shape of a pigeon's feather, together with which the cautery should be;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	If you see it, let it be marked from one end to the other, and if you see it, let it also be like a tent.
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	However, the one that is raised is useful for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After pressing the fistula if it is open, remove the pus and dry it;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	And if it is closed, open it, and draw out the bowels from behind
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	Then place a hot cautery on it and hold your hand on the cautery at the part near the nose above the eye, so that your hand does not become foolish.
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	And put the cautery into the fat of the eye, and burn it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you reach the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, then repeat the cautery once more, and a third time if necessary, and leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	Then put moistened cotton in butter on it, and continue the dry ointment treatment until it is healed. If after forty days it is not healed, apply a corrosive medication until the bone is exposed.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	And the king according to what he would come to his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is one manner of fistulous cautery which some of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Understands that it is a fistula, and opens its path;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Afterward puts into the opening a subtle thread of which this is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	And they make it to the quantity of half a pennyweight.
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	Hold your hand firmly on the thread and do not move the patient's nose so that the molten lead does not run into his eye;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	And it is necessary to put onto the patient's eye moistened cotton in an egg shell or in a sieve:
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	The lead thus seals the path of the fistula and the sore heals miraculously.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have spoken of, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then you must administer a puncture to the nose and return the fistula to its proper place within the nose.
des crevaices en levres	Regarding cracks in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks appear on the lips which are called "cracks," and especially on children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have mentioned in the division of diseases, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cautery scalpel according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And quickly puts it into those cracks until it comes to the front;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterward, treat the wound with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the boil of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess appears at the root of the throat or in the eye, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, afterward it becomes putrid and round and inflamed and becomes a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	And you treat it as we have said in sections, but it is of no benefit:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	Then it is necessary that you apply a cautery according to the size of the fistula.
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	After the cut or puncture of the fistula, hold your hand there until the iron becomes hot at its base and behind it;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And do this once or twice, after treating it as we have said in treatments, until it is healed.
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	If it is cured thus, that is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	And if not, then the site must be opened and the rotted bone removed, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	on toothache
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medications but this does not help, then place the patient's head in your lap;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	After heating the cautery whose shape will be shown below, so that you can place it on the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	And put hot irons quickly inside the cautery, and hold your hand there until the patient feels heat reaching the root of the tooth.
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	Then remove your hand and resume the cautery as you wish;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	Then the patient fills their mouth with salted water, holds it there for an hour, and rinses it out thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth that was loose is made firm again, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupt moisture is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	on toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When tooth pain comes from coldness, or there is coldness or dampness present, and medicinal treatments are ineffective, then cautery is needed in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	And cauterization with butter and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cauterization with butter is done by taking cow's butter, and placing it on an iron or brass spoon;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	Then take cotton, wrap it around the tip of a tent stake, dip it in melted butter, and apply it quickly to the aching tooth. Hold it there until it cools.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	And repeat this often until its effectiveness reaches the root of the tooth. And if you see that the wool and cotton become soaked in cold butter, place it on the aching tooth, and apply hot iron until the fire reaches the tip of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The cautery with fire is thus made: Take an iron or brass tube, and make it thick so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth.
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After heating the cautery, of which the form will come later, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, for the pain will be relieved on that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And the patient should fill their mouth with good butter during the application of this cautery, then remove it.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	Make the cautery according to the size that you desire and according to your ability;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	And this is the shape of the tube:
des scrophules	"of scrofulas"
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the boils are filled with phlegm and cold moisture, and do not yield to digestion by medications, then heat the hair cautery of which the form follows, and let it have two openings for the smoke to escape from the other side.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	Place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice, depending on how deep it is.
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	If the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to its size, and leave it on for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	And place moistened cotton soaked in butter until the burn is healed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, treat it with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cautery:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When moistures gather in the channels of the lungs, especially when it is due to a cold condition, then the patient should first be treated with dissolving medications.
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	Then perform cautery at the root of the throat, taking care not to go all the way down to the throat and not to burn too much of the heart.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	Then perform another cautery at the junction of the neck and the head of the spine, using the cautery called 'clavile', the shape of which is shown above.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heal the wound as we have said before until it is clean.
de la toust	de la toux
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all diseases of the lung are due to cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or shortness of breath, and the disease is chronic, then apply two cauteries on the bladder in suitable places;
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	And place another cautery between the two breasts.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	And let the cautery be of the type called "clavile," according to the form described earlier.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you wish, perform cautery by pricking with all of the cautery called "pointe," the form of which is described earlier in the disease of the ears.
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And let there be up to thirty points, or as many around it.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	Afterward, heal the place according to what is said before, and let there be three rains of cautery according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because these cauteries are easier to perform, you should make three incisions at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	de la dislocation de l'épaule
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the arm bone is dislocated due to moist humors and is repositioned but keeps slipping back and becomes dislocated again even with slight movements, as we have experienced, it is necessary to first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Then have the patient lie on their back and side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	then lift the heart which is inside the titillate with the two fingers of your left hand;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated inside, then heat the cautery that has two points until it is red hot.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	Burn the heart with a cautery until it pierces to the side, and bring together four cauteries at once.
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	And for this reason, cauterize with the cautery that has three openings, so that there are six marks of cauterization.
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	The nerves are as fine as a thread, and it is the shape of the cautery with three openings:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	"And sometimes it is attached above this one nerve, for which there are eight cauteries."
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	Next, apply powdered purslane seeds with honey;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Then let the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated upwards, which happens rarely, then apply cautery on the thickness of the cautery clavile, or many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For once the joint is closed, and moisture removed, the patient is healed
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach causing it to lose its temperament, and there is an increase in phlegm that does not benefit from usual treatments, then the patient must be turned onto their back, extend their legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	Then apply three cauteries beneath the armpit of the arm on each side with the quantity of two digits, so that each cautery is like a key, and two cauteries outside the two sides so that the marks of the cauteries are at three angles, and have such space between them that they do not join together when they discharge pus.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	And let the cauteries be so deep that they pierce both parts of the heart, and let the marks of the cauteries be in this shape without irregularity:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see a large cautery branding on the stomach in this manner;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and whoever fears this cautery should brand with a prick and press it onto the stomach once, according to the size that you see there.
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cauterize with the entire cautery called "the point.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	**After the treatment of the cure that we had before, until it is healthy.**
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When pain in the liver comes from coldness, moisture, and excess windiness, so that its natural composition is impaired by excesses;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is treated as we have said in divisions, but it does not help them, then the patient should be bled from their heel vein.
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and apply three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity onto the liver, avoiding the hypochondria, where the rib of the man comes.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and keep a space between each cautery equal to the thickness of two fingers.
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cauteries be long and thin, and do not press your hand too hard onto all the cautery.
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	And let only half of the cautery burn, and let the patient lie on their right side.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	And if he cannot do so, then he should lie down, extend his legs, and raise his arms.
et c’est li forme:	And this is the method:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if it is your will, then cauterize these cauteries of the scalpel, if you are skilled and wise in the art, but beware that you do not burn all the heart, for you would dry out the whole body.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and let it not come near to the belly, for the heart is very subtle there, and the liver knows for certain.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When he has an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	If it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain but not too strong.
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	And if it is in the membrane, he feels insane pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	Then when this treatment is undertaken by the physicians, the patient must be made to lie on his back.
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then place on top of where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a branding iron; here is its shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize with the cautery until the flesh is burned and bring it up to the skin so that all the pores are opened.
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	After treating according to the treatment of ulcers until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And only those who have studied at length in the art of medicine should use this cautery, and by whose hands these illnesses have often been cured.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore he can boldly work, although it seems better to leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	"of the cautery for pleurisy"
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that for pleurisy one must make cauteries with the roots of aristolochia in this manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a long root of aristolochia, as large as you can find, dry and also as thick and as long as your two fingers;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	And soften it in oil and take it to the fire, and cauterize with the cautery between the navel and the neck, and make two small cauteries a little way down towards the part below the beard.
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	And place two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, sloping slightly downward.
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	And place one cautery in the breast, another above the stomach, one between the two shoulders, and two on either side of the breast, below the cautery between the shoulders.
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	Press your hand not at all, but hold it gently, as when smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And some ancients said that certain people used to use a fire cautery resembling a razor, heat it and place it between the ribs until it reaches the boil.
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	When there is pain, as we have mentioned in the case of a liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear where the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	"of the mouse"
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said in the sections on treatments and it does not improve, then there are three methods of cauterization that are all beneficial.
