et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have ready a sponge and many bandages to wipe away the blood; then insert the forceps at two points, of which this is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	From the incision that starts at the temple up to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	And strip away all the skin that is between the two incisions up to the soft tissue on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision up to the other second one, and then remove this forceps.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Then insert into the first incision the instrument called "the curette", which is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other. Here is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the sharp knife towards the flesh near the heart, and the blunt knife towards the bone, and cut until it reaches the middle groove.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous down to those that open from the heart, then make another cut in the middle incision up to the other end.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	Then drain the blood evenly and press the wound to stop the bleeding;
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	Then place in each incision a wick of old cotton, and put on moist bandages soaked in wine, oil, and honey, ensuring that no abscesses form.
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And on the third day untie the linen, and bring great plenty of cold water, then apply the plaster of balsam with rose oil, and other treatments to heal wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	"of the eyes"
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	If catarrh comes frequently, and you see the eyes thin and small, and weakens sight, and burns the membranes;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair falls out, and deep in the head there is burning pain, and the patient sneezes
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	then know by these signs that those matters and that catarrh come from many veins, and the proper treatment for it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you should command the patient to lie down on their back, then make a long incision along the forehead and another across it.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin at the opening of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be made down to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and keep your hand away from the nerves that move in chewing
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	And when the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, and then open between the two lips of the wound and put in old cotton, and linen strips.
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	Then tie upon cloths moistened in wine and oil, and guard against hot abscesses.
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	When it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying agents that cause the flesh to adhere.
En teil maniere:	In this manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	Take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony; make a plaster from them
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and apply this plaster to these wounds to cause flesh to adhere all around.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of earplugs
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All that falls into ears is one of four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	 either grain, or beast, or stone from a mine, or similar thing like iron.
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seed, such as peas, beans, lentils
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or flowing things like water and juices and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When something like a stone or other thing falls into the ear which does not fit well nor grow in the ear, place the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, then distill some drops of violet oil or sesame oil, and apply it for extraction
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and when the stone is expelled by sneezing, hold the nostrils closed during sneezing, and wrap around the ear cloths or wool.
et estent l’oreille au desus.	And they attach the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times fire comes from this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	And if it does not come out by fire, let him bring about extraction with subtle tweezers, of which here is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it jumps out with the tweezers, that's good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	But if not, then bring about extraction with a small, subtle hook;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	And if it does not come out with that, then make a small copper tube and thrust the end of the tube into the hole of the ear strongly, and stop up what is around the tube with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the tube;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	Then draw fire strongly through it, for often does fire come thus as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	And if it does not come out by fire in this manner, then take pitch with which they catch birds, and put some of it on an instrument that is sharp for this purpose, and place a bit of cotton around it;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the buttock over the stone or whatever it may be, and draw fire.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it does not jump out from all these things that we have said, then hasten to cut the ear before the abscess becomes hot and spasm occurs.
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	And the manner of cutting is as follows: first, make the patient lie on their back, and draw out blood according to the measure of their strength; then have the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear where it depends on fat.
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	And let the cut be like a half-moon until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability and suck it out quickly into your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and continue treating him until he is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is gravel that is inside and it swells, then administer an extraction.
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot come out, then administer a thin, subtle spatula according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision on that boil.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this when you think the grain is moist due to ear moisture.
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	Then extract it with tweezers or forceps gently and carefully, as we have said, so that the extraction is smooth.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	Therefore, in the water that falls into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use sneezing movements first, and plug the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out from there, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If not, then take many thin, light pins according to the length of your thumb and heat them a little over the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and have the patient insert one or two of these pins into a perforation in their ear, with one end sticking out on the other side, and then place another pin on top of the one inside the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and continue doing this from pin to pin until all the water has come out, and thus it will all flow out.
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	And if you see this, then take a reed, insert one end into the ear, and heat the other end with fire until the inner part of the reed is burned.
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	Then repeat this process with other reeds until all the water has come out, as we have said in the case of pins.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In extracting a creature, if it is small-bodied, like a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the section on division.
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	But if it is large-bodied so that one can feel it, then arrange an extraction using forceps;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and this is the easiest thing to remove that might be in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In extracting roundworms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the section on division and dealing with distillations, and if the treatment does not help, then you must examine the ear in sunlight
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	if no worms are visible, use delicate forceps to extract them; if they still cannot be seen, then use the instrument whose shape is shown here
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And insert the most subtle end of the instrument into the ear according to the extent of the patient's suffering, then suck strongly along the entire length of it
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Repeat this often until all the worms emerge.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey and come out, then plug around the instrument with cotton as I have said regarding stones;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	And if they do not leap out as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the killing of worms, and you will find them in treatises on distillations.
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if you distil your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, here is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	It should be made of silver or thin brass below for the small holes, and above for distilling.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	And for pressing inside the distillation, make sure the instrument is well-made of brass, and if you wish, take a razor and wrap cotton around its point carefully.
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	Then pour your oil or juice into the tube, along with any of your medicines you wish in the ear, and place the tube in the ear.
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	Then insert the razor with all the cotton inside, and press gently with your hand until the oil has been distilled into the ear.
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	And let the patient feel it inside; and let the distillation be in a small pot warmed over the fire before it is distilled into the ear.
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And ensure that [the cautery iron] is not too cold, for then the remedy would not be good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of earplugs
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born without any holes in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and the same happens to people due to blockage of wounds or tissue born within the ear, and these blockages sometimes go deep into the ear so they cannot be seen;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	And sometimes there is no hole, yet it can still be seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	So then, if the blockage is deep and cannot be seen, it is difficult to treat in many cases; but if one can see it, then place the ear of the patient towards the sun;
et regarde dedens:	And look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	If you see the operation clearly defined, then perform this procedure according to the form written below:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And let it be sharp and cutting in front and behind, so that it does not wound the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	If the blockage is of flesh or bone within the ear, then hold it with fine forceps and cut gently until all that flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the eruptions are deep in the ear, then take a sharp, light razor and heat it slightly on the fire, then place it on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you sense the obstruction that causes the patient to feel pain upon hearing, pierce it easily and ensure you do not harm the nerves of the ear.
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	Then place in the ear a wick according to the width of the piercing, and soak it in Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this for several days until the wound is healed; then take a wick and soak it in rose water, and sprinkle powdered tartar on it.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	And if you see that the ear is swollen, then you must remove the wick and replace it with another wick soaked in rose oil cerate until the swelling is gone.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then continue treating it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	"And if bleeding begins to flow, then dip a sponge and wring it out in cold water, and place it on the ear. Use other remedies that stop bleeding which are found in treatises on distillation."
de la char des papieres	"de la chair des papieres"
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	These membranes that come from the eyes when they are moist and dry should be stretched out with forceps and tweezers, and cut off at their base with a scalpel.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Then sprinkle powdered tartar on the wound.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if you find blood on the skin, then cauterize it with a small circular cautery iron, and afterwards cut around the incision.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and often they return, unless something remains at their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	Hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times there come forth from the eyes certain things that resemble hail in their shape and hardness, and for this reason this illness is called 'hail', which is a gathering of thick moisture on the paper above and below.
li ovraiges est telz:	The workings are such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	Be aware if the hail moves from one side to the other, and this is easy to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Then make an incision on the large side, gently scrape each part with a scalpel, then grasp it with forceps and cut it off.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you cannot cut it off without piercing the paper somewhat, it does not matter to the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	And if the wound is large, join it with a suture, and treat it until it is healed.
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If it is small, do not exert force, for gentle treatment will restore it quickly and form scar tissue.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the hailstone descends into the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, grasp the hailstone with tweezers, and gently press it from both sides;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is moved away by the incision, that does not matter.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And once the hailstone has been removed, rinse the ear with saltwater, and treat the site where scar tissue formed until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	de la graisse des eulz
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a fatty substance that becomes trapped in the webs of paper tissues above, which happens more often in children than adults. It causes great discomfort to their eyes and they experience watery discharge in the mornings, unable to look at sunlight because tears rush to their eyes.
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	And therefore they often lie on their faces and sleep like that, with their papers wet under their eyebrows, causing swelling and inflammation to cover the exit pupil which opens in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press your thumbs on both sides and feel the exit point between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of working is this: The patient should place his head on your hand;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	Then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains the exit pupil from each part, then place it on top;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	And press with your two thumbs, one on either side, so that the exit pupil is gathered within the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	Then make a cut through the middle of the moisture with a sharp scalpel blade, creating a slit no wider than the wound made when letting blood from a vein;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	And cut deeply into the skin until you reach the exit pupil;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And in many cases, the exit pupil comes out of the slit in the form of a white piece of fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Remove then, with one piece of soft linen between your fingers at the front, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Ensure that you do not insert into the crevice; watch so that all the spatula reaches up to the eye without injuring it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the exit is not at the beginning of the crevice, then slightly widen the crevice lightly until it appears.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	Then remove it as we have said, then moisten rags in warm and cold water and place them on the location, and apply compresses.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are men who crush mustard seeds and place them atop to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healthy again.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms in a hot location, then treat it with soothing plaster until it heals.
des poilz des papieres	Of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When hairs grow on the eyelids that are not natural and become entangled, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases such as habitual tearing and softening of the eyelids, leading to the destruction of the eyes;
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	And there are four methods of treatment:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	Either by cauterization with fire together, or by warm medicine as stated earlier in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by tweezers, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary for you to place the head of the patient in your hand, then twist the paper from the eye towards your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	if it is turned over, that's good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, then insert a needle along the entire thread.
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and this should be done near the edge of the paper where the hairs grow around these hairs, and draw the thread upwards along the entire paper, then twist it towards the razor;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then cut below the paper, below the hairs attached, along the entire blade edge, from the large corner to the small one;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then extract the thread, and place underneath the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth, then press upon the paper with an iron, like a mint leaf, making sure that the pressure is according to the amount you see lifting the paper which has been cut.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if there is need to cut off a large quantity of the paper according to how moistened it is;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	Then make all of the spatula according to the two lines you have marked, beginning from the large handle down to the small one.
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	And let it be one of the slits near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root; then place the unicorn horn at one of the two corners of the heart, and scrape all over.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	Then bring the two lips together with a stitch of fine thread made from wool, and wipe away the blood; and harden the surplus threads over both eyebrows with any sticky substance you have if you wish to do this.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	And if not, pay no heed to it; then leave the stitch and threads for three or four days
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	Then heal the wound without stitching with dry and constricting things, for paper weakens the healing of the wound and its union, but stitching is harmful (as the ancients say), and this is done without fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	And there is another manner:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	It should be that you draw on the paper a figure like the leaf of a myrtle, as we have explained, with three incisions according to the form shown below:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	"Then cut those that exceed the small forces evenly according to the shape shown here."
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you are unable to hold the forceps, and the thing is not even, then take a needle with one thread attached and insert it into the figure;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	And place the second thread next to the large bell, and the third thread next to the small one, and bring together between your two fingers evenly.
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift your hand evenly, and raise all the skin where you have drawn, as we have explained, then bring together the two lips of the wound by stitching, and heal it until it is sound.
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if an abscess forms at your incision, then soothe it with wax and similar softening ointments;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	Sometimes the hairs of the paper are reversed:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	If you must use what we have said about incision.
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	But stitching is more artful on one side than the other.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of sinews follows this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	And take the paper and fold it inside according to what I have said, then make two sinews artificially, and two fine threads as long as the paper and as wide as the span.
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	And cut off two heads of two parts where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	Then bring together both subtly over what is above the paper oil, and tie the two sinews of the two parts firmly;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	And leave it thus for a few days, and the skin that is tied will die, shrivel, and become porous until it falls off.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it takes too long, cut it with forceps, then treat it until it is healthy;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	And when the wound is healed, and the paper has been removed, the hairs will no longer grow.
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	And this is the form of the two cakes which you shall make according to this figure, and according to this quantity in length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The operation is such that you take a thin needle, and through it pass one thread of soft and fine silk;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	Then join the heads and tie them both carefully, with the length of the threads being a palm's length;
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	Then pass another thread of silk through it briefly, tying the ends of the thread;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	The patient then places their head in your hand;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	And be near the sun so that the operation is clear, for it is a subtle and small operation. Then insert the needle along the entire length of the hair root, piercing it quickly through the skin until you draw it out naturally from above the hair;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	Then pull out the hair up to the point where it entered, and pass that hair through the needle if there is one or two or three or more;
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Then pull your hand out so that all the hairs come out with the paper along with their natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the wick has been treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the wick from underneath until all the thread you have wound comes out, so that the wick comes out through the hole above and you can see it by the sight of your eye.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then pull out the wick and thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hairs return to their place and flesh grows over them.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hairs are short, then accompany them with one long hair from your head and let it be lifted with it until it becomes elongated, and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	"About the rottenness of the eye"
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease called "aleacrati" or corruption occurs in the eye, there are two ways to treat it:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	One is natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or cut, or burn, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the manner of the work is this: You should cut through that joint, separate its lips, and insert linen wicks. Then bind it until it heals.
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And you must not use things that dry and constrict in treating it.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, the illness will return worse than before;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	But apply softening things, such as fenugreek.
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And rosewater or alembic and linseed oil boiled, and diacylglycerol melted in some of the oils, wrapped in a linen cloth, for this is the treatment.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the essence of your treatment is to ensure that it does not heal in its former shape;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And these procedures we have mentioned are only remedies for this disease, so that it does not return in the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of flesh that comes into the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is underneath is truly called 'axacrati', and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	Accidents happen from wounds and cuts and burns and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	And the way of the operation in this case is that you take a needle with doubled thread, and insert it into the flesh, making it pierce from the left eyelid as far as the right one, so that the threads come out on both sides of the flesh.
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Then stretch the flesh above along the whole needle, and cut it with a wide spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the figure on the paper returns as it should, that is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	If not, then take a razor and place it in the slit, turn the paper, and make two slits on each side within the paper;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and the openings of the two slits should be at the two corners of the incision you have cut, and one angle should be made so that when they are joined together, the figure is like the figure of a letter called 'I Greek'.
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	Then remove that flesh according to the size of its sides and bottom from what is beneath the paper, then join the two separated parts together and sew them with a wool thread;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, treat those we have mentioned with softening medicines, and use tents until they are healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the disease comes from a cut or stitching or cauterization, then you must make an incision full of pus beneath the hairs of the pubic region, and according to what is written above.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then place between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must perform the procedure according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in shape, and the wise master prepares everything with all his power so that the form returns to its natural shape
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patient himself, according to what is needed in each procedure and tools for various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	Of the suddenness of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this injury happens to many men in such a way that the skin above is stuck with the whites of the egg, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must put the tip of a razor underneath the skin and lift it up.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	And they apply it like pincers, until you grasp what is ready at the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too cutting, so that the patient cannot suffer if the spatula is too sharp and blinds the eye.
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	And let your incision be light, from which you strip away that gathering, so that the skin returns to its natural form;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and all of that gathering is healed, and sometimes they put salted water in the eye, and rinse it with fresh water, and with collyrium;
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then place a linen tent between the skin and the eye, and put wool moistened in egg white over the eye;
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after the third day, apply cold compresses and ointments until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that a nail is in two ways:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	either it is nerve-like and similar to hard skin, or another kind that is not nervous but resembles moist white congealed blood, which when touched by iron and grasped with pincers cannot be seized.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	And both kinds of it start near the large eyelid, and grow little by little until they cover all the sight and light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts their head in your hand, then opens their eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	then lift the paper with your hand, then curl the finger like tweezers of small width, and stretch it over;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	Then take a needle, and put in it a horse hair, or goat's hair, or cow's hair, and strong thread;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the tip of the needle slightly and stick it into the finger, and pierce through with all the needle, and tie the finger with a thread and stretch it over, and scrape all along the hair's edge on the inside of the nail that goes between the skin and the hair up to the top, then cut off the remaining part at the root of the eyelid with a very fine spatula and gentle forceps, and leave the natural flesh of the eyelid so that tears do not flow through the incision as usual.
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	And sometimes the nail stands up on its own and on the string, as we have said.
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	Then scrape off all the fat from this meat; here is the shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And ensure that the spathulum does not touch the delicate tissue and break it, and that the probe is not pierced.
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	And after the incision, pour in a little powdered sage, and make a poultice with litharge, leaving it until the next day.
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat this wound as necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not nerve-like and you cannot insert the needle, and the tweezers will not fit, many times this type of nail can be treated with medications.
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And they grow as I described in the section on division; and if you see them opening, immediately perform the eye of the patient and take a light stroke with the spathulum according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And raise the nail gently upwards, and if you see that it does not decrease in size and the bone presses close afterwards, then distill from your mouth onto a hot coal made of litharge and red ochre ground together, and plug the eye until the next day;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Then begin the other operation according to this same procedure, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is any obstacle in the eye that opposes this operation, such as a hot aposteme, then apply cold compresses and first treat the hot aposteme until it is healed; then resume the operation as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear duct harms the eye greatly, then suspend it with sinew and cut off part of it, but not all of it, so that tears may still come.
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then distill onto the eye red hot coal made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	And regarding the flesh that grows upon the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	In some men's eyes, red flesh sometimes grows, covering the pupil and pressing on the membranes, turning towards the front, resembling awart.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	And the operation is that the patient places his head in your hand, then you open their eyes and coil all of that flesh with suitable tweezers for this purpose, and hold it firmly;
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	Then cut the first hair, and keep cutting all the way down to the skin until finished, but be careful not to wound the eye during the process.
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	And make the incision of the spur small like we said in cutting the nail and the little forces with which one removes the bone, as shown later in this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	And once the incision is complete and all flesh removed, apply to the eye a powdered salve or distill upon it red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines; then place cotton soaked in egg white over the eye so that it may be securely bound with a warm plaster.
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	And if anything remains and the heat increases, and you doubt a hot inflammation, then leave the eye alone and treat the inflammation with things that alleviate heat.
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Then return to your work until it is safe, and so do for every flesh joined in the eye by this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But nevertheless you must align the treatment of each weak eye according to its natural course.
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and in accordance with its accidental course, particularly using iron instruments;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But do not perform any of these operations until you see that the member can withstand them.
des voines des eulz	"of the veins of the eyes"
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Before there are red veins that cover the eye, they veil its work and weaken sight every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is therefore necessary that you first examine whether the eye in which the stone is present is protruding, and if there is no other external disease besides the stone;
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then treat it in this manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Instruct the patient to place their head on your lap, then gently compress those veins on both sides according to your discretion, and make the bandage thin and doubled in this manner:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	"And there should be two bandages placed at intervals along one course according to this shape:"
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then gently compress those veins thusly, and wipe away the blood immediately afterwards, until you see that the veins outside the eye are retracted;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	And ensure that you do not cut the eye with the points of the forceps, and perform this operation at midday facing the sun, being very careful in your work so that you do not injure anything but those veins;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	And once you have done this, then distill in the eye green and red collyrium to corrupt what remains of the sediment.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you are unable to collect all of this at that hour, then make a plaster for the eye with soothing substances for the pain in the eyes, and leave it on for several days until the pain is alleviated and the heat of the abscess is assured, then resume according to this manner which is written before until it is healed.
et c’est li forme des forces:	And this is the form of the poultice:
de la fistule de l’oil	"of the fistula of the eye"
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The surgeon calls a fistula 'arissati'
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When you treat it with cautery and with burning hot medicine as I said before, and it is not yet healed, then know that there is something inside which you should incise over the abscess where it must be cut open, and draw out all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, then you must use all of the instruments mentioned here for its form:
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and is called 'sharp head', and it should be made of iron from the crown downwards, and should be pointed like a file as it is in its current form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And place on the location of the rotten bone, then twist it between your fingers and press gently until you feel that the corruption is removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this several times, then apply drying medicines to the location.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the location is solid and flesh grows back, and the body of the bow is solid, and remains thus for forty days, and it does not renew itself nor become infected, and no bad accident occurs, then know that it is healed;
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If not, then there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nose according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and that you uncover the bone a second time with iron and hot medicines, and when it is uncovered take the chisel according to this form, with an iron head having three angles, and the handle tapered all the way to the tip as shown here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	Then place it on the bone near the ear, and keep your hand away from the eye. Then turn the drill until it pierces the bone; the patient will feel this because the vein will then flow out if their hand is on their nose.
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	Then restore the place with dry medications as I have taught you. When the flesh grows and the joint hardens, then go to the nose.
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	It is easier for the patient this way.
de l’issue de l’oil	Regarding the issue from the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eye opens completely in every direction and there is no obstruction to the nose or diminution, then you must bandage the patient.
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	Then wash the eye, then apply cupping glasses without touching to suck, then place on the eye a linen made of acacia and aloe and incense and saffron, then compress the eye, and cover it with bandages and cloths.
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	And the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths and fold each one into four layers, then place them on top of each other according to how much the eye needs.
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	Then tightly bind it with a firm bandage from above, and resume using cupping glasses to suck without striking.
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	then remove the cupping glasses and keep the eye bound day and night; if it begins to loosen, then you must bind it tightly.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	Then remove the bandage after a day and night, and if you see the eye improving, that is good;
se ce non;	if not
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	then resume the emplastrum, dressings, binding, and cupping glasses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Regarding the bursting of a blood vessel in the eye
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When disruption comes to the uveal membrane, then it appears, and fire comes out of the papers like grains of resin, which is frightening to see.
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	Then if you see it covered, the procedure is such that you insert a needle into the root of the part below until it reaches the part above, then insert another needle where there is a doubled thread on the eyelid.
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and pierce it through, leaving the first needle in place according to its position;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	Then cut the spot with the double thread and tie one part of the vein around it, pulling it taut; then remove the needle and place a wet linen cloth moistened in egg white over the eye.
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and let it remain until the threads adhere with the vein; then heal the eye with comforting substances until the wound is healed.
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And sometimes the wound is held in place by each vein being bound with a circle of cloth until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eye appears swollen, then pierce it with a fine spatula that comes from within the eye, and correct the moisture in the white of the eye, allowing it to descend; then insert it quickly.
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	Regarding the bowing of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but mucus gathered in the eye, resembling descending water, and it is not water.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	The appearance of this disease is that you make the patient sit on an arranged and upright seat; then take their head between your two hands, and tilt it until you see the mucus come up to your eyes.
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	Then let it be inserted, and not descend, and let the light be extinguished, and let the patient see things as they used to.
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend below, know that it is acute, and if the descent of the bowel is not as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	Have the patient sit between your hands, then take the spatula and cut through the corneal membrane near the junction of the conjunctiva with the cornea and sclera until the bowel emerges.
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And once it is out, distill hot water mixed with honey or boiled fennel and honey onto it, then dress it further until it is clean.
des aigues de l’oil	Regarding the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have here the signs of acute [disease] in division, and those which ought to be pierced.
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if you work according to the patient's condition.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	You must have the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from sunlight, with the healthy eye tightly closed and held firmly.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	Then place the eye paper on your left hand if the eyes are left [ones], or on your right hand if they are right [ones];
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	Then take in your left hand, if the eyes are left ones, the instrument called "almagda," or in your right hand, if they are right ones.
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then place the tip of the instrument near the cornea by the thickness of a grain at the part below the inner corner of the eye, then gently insert the instrument called "almagda," turning your hand until it pierces into the white of the eye, and feel that almagda reaches the empty space.
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	And it is necessary that the length of the almagda's pathway be equal to the distance from the pupil up to the end of the blackness.
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	And this is the cornea of the eye.
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	If you see the bone through this paper due to the clarity of the corneal tissue, then move the instrument until it reaches where the water is, then press down along one vein after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water rises now, then the patient sees before them and the instrument in their eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After a short rest, if the water rises up the second pathway, place the funnel with the instrument, and when it is inserted and it does not rise, then gently remove the almagdah in a twisting manner bit by bit.
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then add a drop of blue silk to the water, and rinse the eye with it inside and out.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place before the eye plugs made of wet wool in rose oil and egg whites, binding it with healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, we and those of our time place commin broie upon it with plenty of eggs.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, because there are certain people who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	Therefore, pierce only the conjunctiva, not too deep but carefully; then insert the almagdah as we have said.
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	And upon completion of the procedure, prepare a comfortable bed for the patient to lie on his back in a dark place
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and keep him still from all movements; let him eat light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left. Bind him according to his condition for three days
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then untie him in the same dark room, examine his vision, and show him some things to look at. Then reapply the bandage for seven days
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And it is not necessary that you do this during or after the incision now, but rather you should tie off that vessel, because water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	If an abscess becomes hard, untie the eye before the seventh day, and apply what subdues the abscess;
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	And once it has subsided, untie the bandage and place a compress soaked in honey to cover it for several days, keeping it always in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	Then slowly exit the house little by little, and return to his usual activities;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one from Iraq came to us and said that in his land people used to make something called 'almagda' for piercing, through which water is extracted. However, I have never seen any such thing in our land nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And perhaps it's something new.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the likenesses of the forms of algebra, so that those who do not know them may see them;
et soient d’arain proprement:	and they should be made of pure silver:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their heads should be of this same subtlety, and the back in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	Here are some ways to treat flesh growing on the nail:
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Sometimes nails or horseshoes are born twisted in various ways, among which some resemble scorpions with many feet;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	And there are also such ones where the iron has enchanted hair of dark color, and the skin has soft hair of fair color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	Therefore, in the case of a horse that is gentle and not enchanted, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open his nostrils, and throw the unicorn's horn at those horses, and draw them apart strongly;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	until you can no longer support it on the subtle point of the compass needle on one side, until you know that the horse is completely exhausted.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if anything remains that cannot be coped, then open it with all the subtle tools lightly, so that nothing remains;
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	And if blood does not mount up, or a hot abscess appears, then cut as it is necessary.
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if it is malignant abscesses, then hurry and cauterize until the blood is stanched and all the flesh is removed, then pour on quicklime and vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If nothing happens, and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is incurable;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	And if moisture does not reach as it should, know that there is flesh grown into the bone above, to which the instrument cannot come to cut:
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	Then you must insert a thread of fine linen, slightly thickened with our hands, and have it dampen between each knot.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	And let the patient place the head of the thread in his nostril with some force, and pull on it with care until it comes into the mouth.
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	Many children do this at school, and it is an easy thing for one who wishes to do it;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	Then grasp the head that comes from the snow with one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and pull them apart gently one after the other, following our method which they are in.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you know that the nerves have corrupted that flesh, then pull out the threads, squeeze out the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian gum, and replace it in the snow as before;
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Do this for three days or more, until the poultice has corrupted all that remains of the flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	And then place in the snow a cake of lead for several days until it is dry, and if there is need for drying medications, use them.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, where oils and medications are distilled in the snow:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it should be made of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a pipe, with the conduit also.
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	And if you see one, make a closed cane and let the instrument be full to purge the head.
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And have many hands at the head to hold it when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Here are some ways to treat flesh growing on the nail:
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times there arises on the head a disease called "telul", which grows and becomes large continually until it is visible to look at.
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	And therefore you must cut it off at the beginning, and scrape away all fur, then place on level the cautery or burning medicine.
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	But if one delays cutting until it is large, take heed whether it is hard, of dark color, and lacks sensation:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	If not touched by iron for it is an enchanted abscess; for when one cuts it, great harm comes to the patient.
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	But if the abscess is soft to touch, not dark in color, and you see that it can be completely cut out, then let the patient empty and cut it without fear, and cure the area with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	"When the boil is cut and closed"
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know this: when humors accumulate in one of these joints, they profit little there, especially in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is therefore necessary when this happens to anyone, to look whether the wound is fresh with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then join the two lips together in a stitch, and then treat it until it is healed.
