et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	And if the lips are already separated on both sides, then you must cauterize all parts of their edge until they heal, then join the two lips together in a stitch, and bind it, and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood powder and ground incense.
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place over the powders a piece of strong plaster or another sticking plaster, and leave it until it adheres by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The method of stitching is that you bring together...
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or by needles, as we have said in the abdominal suturing.
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or by thread, as I have shown you.
des apostemes des levres	"boils on the lips"
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	Many people have hard tumors inside the lips, resembling grains of millet, small and large;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	Then it is necessary for you to turn back the lips, and cut along each nostril, and grasp it with forceps and cut in every part.
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	Then fill the space after the incision with powdered vitriol until the blood is stanched.
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then the wound should be stitched up, and the area dried with dry cloths until it is clean
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Often there appears on the fleshy gum a growth called "albulus" by the ancients;
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	then you must hold it with forceps and cut at its root, allowing the vein or blood to flow freely
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then apply powdered vitriol or other restrictive and drying powders to the area
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if that flesh returns after being cut, which often happens, then cut it a second time and cauterize it
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return after cauterization
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	And these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of boils
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Some times they are assembled at the head of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, scars which are ugly and sharp.
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	And sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish-green and worm-ridden, such that corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth smell bad.
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	Thus you should make the patient sit between your hands, and their head be in your lap, and scrape the teeth where the scars appear, until nothing remains.
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	And thus do likewise for the blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other stains, until they are cleaned.
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	And if one removes what is at its root cause, it is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	If not, then recommence on the second and third day, until you have scraped all.
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	And know that teeth require various forms of tools to scrape, according to what the task shows, for those used to scrape between teeth have different shapes than those used to scrape on teeth.
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	And these forms and others are to be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	When treating a toothache, delay pulling the tooth as long as possible, for this should not be done at all;
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it is a very high substance until there is no excuse for extracting it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained by thirst, you must be certain of the tooth that is aching.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Often the pain leaves the patient and they believe it is in a healthy tooth, so they have it pulled;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	but still the pain does not depart for that reason, since the evil has already been extracted, as we have seen in many cases.
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	And when you are certain about the aching tooth, then it is necessary to scrape around it with a scalpel, deeply enough to protect the gum from all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then move it gently with your fingers or fine pliers at first, until it is well loosened, then firmly grasp it with the forceps;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	And hold the patient's head between your knees so that they cannot move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take any of these instruments and put it gently on each side, and with the lever move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if a tooth is pierced and eaten away, then you must fill it with wadding where the hole is.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	And if he grasps it subtly with pliers, that it may not break while extracting;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And one must operate much around the gum to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And see to it that you do not break it, and if a piece remains, it will cause the patient greater pain due to the root's mischief.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not act like the ignorant surgeons who through their haste and boldness sometimes break the cheekbone, and do not bring about what we have mentioned;
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but by their carelessness, great diseases sometimes occur due to the roots that remain there, or because of the cheekbone they break, as we have often seen;
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	And when the tooth is pulled out, wash the place with wine, vinegar, and salt.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	And if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill the place with powdered vitriol;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shapes of the instruments with which one moves the teeth first should be long-pointed and have thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth.
et ce sont les formes:	and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of large limbs so that they do not bend at all during traction, and let them be of iron well-made, and let them be toothed for holding movement.
de la racine des dens	Of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains in place during tooth extraction, you must apply cotton moistened with butter for one or two days until the area is softened, then insert the forceps called "algefree", so that the head appears like a bird's beak.
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and they should also be shaped within like a file, which is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	"And if the roots do not wish to come out with all these pliers, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root, and place the instrument called 'althali', that is, the crowbar, of which this is the shape:"
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root comes out by itself, that is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If not, then use all the instruments, whose shapes are shown hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	"And if one uses this tool that has two handles, of which this is the shape:"
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	"and other iron tools that are before in the reason of the teeth, and of this tool that resembles large pliers, of which this is the shape:"
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let this instrument be strong so that it cannot break, and know that there are many instruments for teeth.
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments which are not enumerated
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And the wise master finds his instrument by himself, according to what his works and the illness reveal, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument due to the diversity of ailments. And if he breaks a bone or others, where it is necessary, then he seeks the instruments that are required, as I have told you, and helps with gestures; this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be large and well-fitting to hold the bone so it doesn't slip away, but can grasp and remove it;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And then restore it to its place with appropriate medicine, and if there is rot in the bone, even if it's small, remove it with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When teeth appear not according to the natural body, and their form is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth is near the other tooth, but not in the right place, and cannot be removed or filed:
adonques lou raie;	then pluck the hair
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is hard with the teeth, then take this instrument of which there is the form below, and it resembles a small beak, and be made of iron well sharpened at the end
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	"And tap the tooth lightly every day for several days to soften it and so that you do not move the others. And if it is apparent enough to be filed, then file it with such a file as this one has here its shape:"
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is also like the file used to make needles.
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	file the teeth gently little by little over several days so that they do not move until they fall out
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then finish it off with any plain razor at the end, and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, then file down its sharpness until it is even so that it does not hurt the tongue or hinder speech
quant li dent lochent	"When teeth lock"
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When a tooth is knocked out in front, either by impact or by falling, and the patient cannot chew their food without it hurting them, and you have treated it with constricting medicines but to no avail
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	then tie it with a gold thread, for silver wire turns green and decays, but gold does not change
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	And let my son's thread not be too thick nor too thin, according to the width of the space between the teeth.
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	And if you see the teeth aligned, then take the thread and a doubled needle between two healthy teeth, and place the heads of the needles between the misaligned teeth, one or more, until you reach bleeding up to the next healthy tooth on the other side.
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	Then resume the threading up to the point where you began, and gently pull your hand steadily until there is no movement.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	And let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut off the heads of the thread with pliers, join them together, and pass them between the healthy tooth, placing them in such a way that they do not injure the tongue.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	Then leave it as tight as possible without causing harm, and if it loosens or the thread breaks, then bind it with another thread.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it remains thus and serves this way throughout its time, then that is the shape of teeth and the direction of growth of the two upper and two lower teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when a tooth falls out, it should be put back in its place, little by little, as we have said.
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and let not the foolish and impatient meddle with it, and sometimes a tooth made of cow bone is used, placed where the gap is, and secured as we have said, and it remains thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	"To cure the tie of the tongue"
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes this tie comes from below the tongue at birth;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by chance due to a healed wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the operation is such that you open the patient's mouth and place their head on your lap, and lift their tongue
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cut the nerve tie from behind until the tongue is freed from its attachment, and if there is scarring or hard tissue, due to an old wound, then insert a hook and cut it away.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	And ensure that the cut is not too deep, for the artery below.
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	Once done, lift up warm rosewater and vinegar, or cold water, then place a linen cloth beneath the tongue.
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	And have the patient apply this every night so that the wound does not dry out.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	If blood comes flowing out, then place crushed vitriol on the location.
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the blood does not clot, cauterize it with the slow-acting cautery, which is good for this purpose.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	If you see a boil that is red or black or hard, even if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	If it leans toward blenching and has moisture, sprinkle onions there, cut it with a fine spatula, and open it on both sides.
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	And if your blood fails you during your work, grind vitriol and apply it until it is staunched; then return to your work until all bleeding has stopped.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then lift the bandage and dressing, and treat with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Here is a translation of the text you provided about swollen glands in the neck:
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes bits of stone appear in the throat which are called 'godaths'; properly speaking they are called the two amygdalae. When you treat them as we have described in this section and yet they do not heal, then be cautious:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If they are hard abscesses with a small opening and dark red color, then do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if they are red and the root is large, then do not touch them with iron; likewise for the flow of blood.
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let it be until it rots, and then you will divide it, or else it would burst by itself;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is white and the root is thin, then prepare the instruments to cut; but first check whether the abscess is warm, rests quietly, and is quieted.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then seat the patient before the sun, their head in your hand, and they open their mouth, and the servant takes it between his hands, and presses down on the tongue with all the instrument; this is the form:
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	And it should be made of silver or fine brass, like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	While pressing the tongue with this instrument, if you see the boil, then take the awl and pierce it into the almond, and draw it forth from above as far as you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	And pull out some cloth with it, then wipe the instrument clean; this is the form that resembles a sieve:
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Moreover, their ends are curved and turned towards each other, and they are very sharp, and made of iron or brass;
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	"And if you do not have this instrument at hand, cut it with pincers, which are shaped thus:"
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And on one side it is sharp, and on the other blunt:
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And once you have cut one boil, then cut the other in the same manner, and afterwards the patient should gargle with hot water mixed with salt, and if blood flows copiously, then the patient should gargle with water in which cooked pomegranate rinds or myrtle leaves have been steeped, until the bleeding stops;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then perform the treatment until it is healed.
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat besides the tonsils; cut them accordingly like the tonsils.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that had grown inside her throat; namely, a small abscess.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And the throat was almost entirely closed, so that the woman could hardly breathe because of the obstruction, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died within two days had it remained thus.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had already risen so much that it had filled both passages of the throat with two raindrops each.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	So I promptly made an incision with a scalpel on one side, then extracted a large portion of the boil.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	Then I reopened the other side of the abscess and opened its mouth, pressing down the tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	Afterward, I cut into these abscesses with a scalpel, cutting off part of them, and only a little blood came out.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	And thus the woman's throat passage was opened again, and she began to drink water and then wine. And I continued to cut into that abscess for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	And the abscesses kept cropping up again, filling the space I had emptied out until they became very large.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	So then I pierced it and cauterized it inside its throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	Thus it remained without growing any further.
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I departed from these parts, not knowing what God did with him afterwards.
de l’uve	"de l'uve"
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When rheum descends to the eye and it is inflamed and protuberant, it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	And if it is below large and round, it is called "eyeball".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When the eye is treated as we have said in the section on division, but the treatment does not help at all, and you see that the inflammation has subsided, and it remains subtle, then you must pierce it.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	And that which is round and gathered together without being protuberant;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	And if it is blood-red or dark-colored or black, then you must avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient in doing so.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is therefore necessary, when you see it according to the manner I have spoken of, regarding its blemish and length, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument whose memory we have mentioned earlier;
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the awl into the eye, and draw it downwards, and cut with one of the two instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the two eyelids.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not cut further than the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cut more, you harm both sight and speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, apply what we have said about the cutting of the two eyelids, until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears being cut, then you must use a device for cauterization to alleviate their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The method of cautery is sharp and hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient places his head in your hand, and then you press his tongue with the instrument mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and heat the forceps with live coals so that it is neither too thick nor too clear;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And when using this tool, of which the form follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And it has at its head a small vessel where one places the medicine, like the head of a spoon, and sets the tool upon all the medicine on the ulcer;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	And let the patient lie on their side so that saliva and mucus from their mouth do not mix with the medicine, so it does not reach the throat or the lung.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the ulcer for about half an hour until you see it is darkened and the absorption of the medicine is complete;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	And if you see, take cotton and wrap it around some tool, wet the cotton in the medicine, and place the tool against all the cotton in the vein until the cotton adheres to the ulcer;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	And do this often until the cautery is complete, then let it dry and fall off after four or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to recommence the cautery of the medicine, then recommence it, and afterwards wipe around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, cleansing that which is around the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be rinsed with cold water, and be cured with gargles until it is clean
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is better than the incision or cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	If it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and marjoram and similar herbs, and combine them all or some of them in one pot, and put it on the fire to boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot has an iron comb made in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And be of silver or brass, and one of the heads be placed in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is anesthetized;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	After the inflammation begins frequently until the eye becomes dry, and ensure that you do not perform this at the onset of a hot abscess formation, for many things can happen there.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not do it except when declining a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, then take a cane and put at its tip an eggshell, so that the mouth of the patient does not become too hot.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the eggshell does not let much steam harm the mouth, and this is a good remedy together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times an object like a bone or fish spine becomes lodged in the throat;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	Therefore you must pull out what you can see and press the tongue down with the instrument so that you can see the object move;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	And what you cannot see and is stuck in the throat, make the patient vomit before the food becomes cooked in the stomach.
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	By chance, if the thing were to go bad through vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	Or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	And ties it to the sponge with thread, and then swallows it
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	And when it comes to its place, so it will harden, and then pull it out
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	And if it does not come out through what we have said, then take the instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it may more easily enter into the throat, and have its head raised high
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	And take care not to touch the epiglottis, that all the way may go down, nor push the bone in
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	But let the patient move the instrument there, so that he knows where the thing is stuck;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	Then push it down until you pull it out evenly with the whole instrument, until it comes out entirely.
de la sansue de la gorge	Here's a possible translation for "de la sansue de la gorge":
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	No bloodletting is performed, as I mentioned earlier in this section;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	And if this does not help, then examine the throat of the patient towards the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument I have mentioned.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see blood vessels, then draw them out little by little with tweezers, or with fine forceps suited for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if bleeding does not help, then take a cane tipped with iron and put it into the patient's throat, then put at the tip of the cane a hot piece of iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	If the patient sweats all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then take a full view of cold water, open the mouth, pour it in without letting them swallow, and move it with your hand frequently.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And as soon as the blood feels the water, it falls.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida using the instrument mentioned in the fumigation of the eye.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times until it falls without staining.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the method of fumigation is as follows: take a pot containing live coals and place it on a stand covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and insert the head of the instrument into this hole.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then cast your fumigation upon it, and the patient places the head of the cane in his mouth, closing the mouth so that no smoke escapes, but reaches the sinew.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and if the sinew does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and let the patient suffer thirst and eat salty foods but drink no water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Then it will be necessary for him to evacuate heat through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	The shape of the instrument used to treat the sinew appears, when visible, like curved tongs for entering into the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and it resembles a goose's beak and is rough like a file, so that what it grasps it cannot let go.
et vez ci la forme:	Here is the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	Chapter on Abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many types of abscesses are described hereafter in this book, differing in perforation and incision;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	And this is of two kinds, one like itself, and what it holds moist.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the places where they occur on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and those on fatty tissue are different from those that come in joints; each has its own judgment in operation.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	But some abscesses should not be pierced until the bowels have died according to their completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are those which must be pierced when they are ripe and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses occur near joints and are left until they are completely surrounded by pus, sometimes the ligaments and nerves of the joint become corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	When the abscess is near the main member, if you delay piercing it until it has died, it will harm the main member;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	Or when it's near the fundament, pierce it before it dies.
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	And do not pierce a ripe abscess without completing its digestion except for the one near the fundament lest it rotted internally and create a fistula.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And you must know the time to pierce an abscess that has died according to its completion when the pain is appeased and the fever departs, and the decrease of pain and redness, and the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs.
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	And you must make the incision where the abscess is most dependent and where it opens moved.
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And let the incision be long along the body; and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and near arteries, and in all places equal where there is no wrinkling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In cases where it pleases, according to this member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the flesh, it is best that you delay their perforation until they are firm and digestion is complete, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	But if you pierce it before that time, then the body will be extended with its venom, and it will be filled with much filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	And perhaps the lips become hardened and the depth of it becomes difficult
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And some abscesses should be pierced according to the width of their body, according to what the member requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And you must bring for small abscesses, small incisions;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and for large abscesses, large incisions, and many slits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	And if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to chop with the knife, and cut;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	When they have become like a blister and are deadened, then you must do as one does for boils
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	And there are such ones which are split into three angles; and there are also such ones which are cut like the cap of a fir tree, as abscesses in the armpits.
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And there are those where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those which have no head, like a soft superficial abscess, must be pierced directly.
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	And when the abscess is large and has formed much bow, you should pierce it but not draw out all of the bow at that time, but only a part.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	Then plug the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more afterwards;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this several times gradually increasing it until all of the bow comes out;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Even if the patient is of weak strength, or a pregnant woman, or young children, or elderly feeble men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	Because sometimes the spirit leaps with the release of the bowstring, causing the patient to die unexpectedly.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore approach this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, then open the wound and observe if the wound from the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	And if it is a simple cut, then bring linen or old cotton pads.
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	And if it's a large abscess with many holes, you must insert a pad into each so they touch each other.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	And if you have cut off a piece of skin from the abscess and shaved around it, then fill it with dry cotton or linen cloth lint without moisture, and bind it for three days.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then bone-set, and apply ointment until healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your procedure, bring cold water and a basin, wet a cloth in it, and place it on the bleeding area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the bleeding persists, bring medical care and treatment, and apply the powders mentioned earlier in this book, especially during wintertime when the affected area is very tense. Then place warm, moist cloths soaked in wine and oil on top of pads.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if it is during summer and the area is fleshy, then place moist cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, for three days, as we have mentioned.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then remove the abscess and heal it, as is necessary, until it is sound.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And these things he should know universally in treating abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	As I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, here is that chapter.
des soros	Here are some key points about boils (soros):
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	And small boils come from the head, and they are like those on hens' wattles, appearing in large numbers.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are fatty and such where there is moisture like feathers;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	And there are some that are hard and stony at the cut, and there is no doubt that an artery opposes it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And this is how one performs the procedure of amputation: first, test all instruments called 'entromissoires', from which the form comes that follows, and what they contain.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	But if it contains moisture, then open it carefully over a long period.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture has been drained, scrape off without leaving any skin that contains this moisture, for it returns immediately if anything is left.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if available;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If not, then in water and salt, and use it to dress the wound, leaving it until the next day.
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And these things will run their course for those that remain of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then resume with cotton as before on the second day and the third, until you are sure there is no more left of the night.
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound with suitable ointment until it is clean.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the swelling holds firm and fat, cut it according to this shape, long;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and cast your onionskins thereupon, and scrape off all around it, and take great care to draw out the coat wherein it lies.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the artery opposes you, then do as I told you afterward.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And similarly, cauterize an abscess if it is hard, cut it open, and treat it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cutting into a hard and moist abscess is easier, since there is little blood involved.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if some of these swellings have no moisture at their head, and those old swellings that I cut off from the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	I found the swelling like a hard, sharp, white stone, and could not be broken.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if one had tried to strike it, they would have made as great a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other swellings that come on the head, besides those which come on the heads of children and at the roots of ears, let the opening always be made in the lowest place possible, so that the bowels may more easily issue.
et les cure si com il covient.	And heal them as it is necessary.
des scrophules	"of scrofulas"
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur at the neck, and under the armpits, and among the anus, and sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and are numerous, and are interconnected.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each boil is properly located within its own skin, like the naevus and the abscess of the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and there are many similar kinds of these boils.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are evil ones that do not wish to obey healing.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	In the one that you see with good position to touch, and is similar in color to the body, and moves from each side and is not hard against the nerves of the neck nor the artery nor the channel, and is not deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	then you should cut it from above and scrape each part, and stretch the two lips of the wound once, if necessary, as we have said about abscesses on the head;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	And cut it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and that the scalpel is not too sharp or cutting too deep, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut a vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work, then place powdered vitriol or some powders that stop blood in the wound, and press the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound begins to soften and rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood is stopped, return to your work until you complete it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Then look at your finger for any small scabs, and cut them off and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scab, then you should not cut off that scab at its base, but tie it with a strong doubled thread and let it fall off without harm;
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then fill the wound with thick cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then bandage it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the entire scab, then it is necessary that you join the two lips of the wound and sew them now, so that there remains no excess due to the size of the scab.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you must understand to cut the root of it, and draw out fire, and stitch as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scabs that hold excess fluid, prick where they open and die;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	And pierce it thus as the one mentioned before, depending on it; then apply dressings with salve and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the wound is well cleaned, treat it internally with ointment until it is healed.
de squinance	de squinance could refer to "squinance" in Old French, which means "a kind of skin disease, scrofula".
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients said and spoke of cutting the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw it done in our land, and that is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have choking fits, the fold of the throat called 'epiglottis' must be cut;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and help should not be given because all the veins and organs of the patient are hot due to an abscess in the mouth or throat.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the membrane, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is therefore necessary that when we want to cut the epiglottis, we do so below three circles or four with a small slit across between two circles, or through its length, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And these places are so close to the epiglottis that there is no flesh there, and the vessels are long on either side.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, then he should stretch the skin of the neck all around the goiter before cutting through it until it reaches the jugular vein.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	Avoid the blood vessels if you see any, and then cut the sciatic nerve as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by cutting the vein of the goiter which suddenly gushes forth from its broken place, and by loss of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	Leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed during which strangulation is feared, join together both lips of the wound around the heart and sew it up entirely without cartilage.
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then administer medicines that promote the growth of healthy flesh.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that this procedure should not be done unless the patient's throat is completely blocked and they are judged to be near death, otherwise there will be damage.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore cut off the epiglottis because the patient cannot swallow and breathes through the wound, thus avoiding death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And for this reason the ancients commanded that the wound should be left open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded that the wound be sewn up and dressed, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a damsel take a knife and stick it in her throat, cutting some of the vessels there.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was called to heal her, but found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I examined the wound and saw that blood had come out of it, and I knew that she had not cut her veins or arteries except for those in her throat, from which the windpipe was protruding through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried and sewed the wound, and cared for it until it was healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	And nothing happened to the damsel except that her voice became hoarse, and afterwards she returned to her former state.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore I say there is no fear in cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of a large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This swelling is called 'throat hernia,' and is a large swelling of yellowish color, common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	And there are two kinds:
naturez, et accidens;	Essences, and accidents;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Or natural has no engine.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And accidents are of two kinds; one is similar to flesh that grows on us, and the other kind is like an abscess that comes from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, but one should not operate with great fire except in the case of a small one; prove and search through all the introitor.
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it like other flesh and not connected to any vein, cut it, as one cuts flesh, and remove all of its skin if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And search well around it, and heal it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	fatty tumors
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many kinds of flesh, all of which I will describe their likenesses;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now I must explain the difference between flesh and bone.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that bone is hot and holds fever until boiling has passed, and corruption is complete;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Then let fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	Without pain, heat, or fever, the nut has no sweat, and contains a white fluid that is like its own sack, matching the color of the body, beginning as a drop, then growing large;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And they are according to two appearances: either fatty or moist, and many have colors as mentioned in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to treat dislocation, first examine and inquire about all the instruments called "intromittent" according to how their forms come in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of examining nasal abscesses is to press on the moistest area you find in the abscess, turning your fingers bit by bit until you know that the instrument has pierced the skin, then proceed according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then remove the trocar, ensuring nothing jumps out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If running moisture is found, regardless of its color, open it as mentioned for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if no moisture comes after the trocar, know that it is fatty, so cut it in a cross shape, grasp it with forceps, and lightly scrape each side, then carefully remove the coating where it rests without harming the nut.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot draw it out whole, then draw it out piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	If anything remains, the wound will reopen many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if some remains and the blood bothers you, then sprinkle the wound with certain watery corrosive powders, bind it tightly, and apply warm soothing things to the inflammation, and continue treating it until it heals;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if the wound is large, cut the two lips of the wound, and treat those that are near flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	And if a beating vein is against you or other such, then quickly apply powdered vitriol to the wound's location, leave it for two or three days until the wound rots, and let the blood's ebullition rest;
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to cauterize what remains of the wound.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Here are the forms of exploratory instruments, and they come in three types:
grans et moien et petit;	Great, medium, small
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	And there are 3 pieces called "albarets", and 1 called "breb", of which there are three kinds:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	 large, medium, and small to encircle the fistulas' abscesses;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	 and are also like the needles used to sew wounds; they are made of yellow brass or iron or silver, with those that are yellow being more valuable, and are particularly preferred for encircling the curves of fistulas
et sont de III manieres:	 and come in three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 large, medium, and small according to the size of the holes' width.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	 The shapes of the forceps are very similar, as you can see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	 Large, medium, and small
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	 And there are also forceps with two curves in three types:
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	 And there are also forceps that have three curves and come in three kinds
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	 And there are also forceps with two curves, and those with only one curve, which come in three kinds
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of these knives are sharp, and there are some that cut only on one side, from which we strip the nerves to avoid cutting the vein or nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And these trocars are those placed in handles so that the patient does not notice them during the opening of abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	And they come in three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	Large, small, and medium-sized, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	And they should only be used in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, angles, and similar locations;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	Moreover, another small instrument resembling the skin of a fist is made according to this form, with which blood is wiped away:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	"And it is sometimes placed at the site where there is danger of cutting veins or arteries, and some are made in this large size:"
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of certain men swell when they begin to be corrupted, appearing like those of a woman;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain unsightly and swollen; anyone wishing to treat them should follow this form from line .b. to .g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scrape away the fat, fill the wound with medication between layers of flesh, then bring together the two lips of the wound to stitch them closed, and treat it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast hangs down and is enlarged like in some women, cut it open through two similar incisions on top.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one holds onto the other at the end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this shape: .b. up to line .g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape away the skin between the two lips and remove the fat. Apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and do whatever is necessary in treating it until it heals.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it does not heal, or the incision is not complete because the patient refuses to rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And let him chew on the remaining flesh and fat until it is clean.
des apostemes des asselles	"Boils in the armpits"
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	"These boils that appear under the arms are hard, with knots, and some contain moisture."
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	He who contains moisture must have the following form cut from the line .b. to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when all the matter inside the boil has been emptied out, then fill the wound with cotton wool and leave it until the following day, then remove all the cotton wool and dress it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed."
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	"If the boil resembles a scrofula, then incise it as we have said for scrofula incisions, and if the wound discharges matter, then apply a cautery as we have said before."
de la routure de l’artere	"Surgical procedure for arterial bleeding"
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When an artery bursts and the skin above is burned shut, many abscesses often form; likewise with a swollen vein and an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if one recognizes it as such when it is for the artery, then the abscess will be long and deep.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	When you sense it with your fingers, you feel tension.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And when it is for the vein, it appears swollen and dark-colored
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	And it is foolish to cut into this abscess, especially when it is located under the armpits and groin areas or in the neck and many other places where it would be very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, one must avoid cauterizing with fire and also the person in charge should avoid doing so, especially when it is an inflammation of an artery that has burst through the skin over a long period.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then make an incision at the joints and carefully separate the artery from the tissues until it is exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then place a needle beneath one side, and pierce it until it reaches the other side, and tie off the artery with a doubled thread in two places, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then prick the place between the two ligaments with an introjector until the blood flows out that is there, and let the abscess be lanced.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then perform the treatment as in a bowed inward wound, until the ligament falls off.
