puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then heal the wound with medicines, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and order the patient to eat heavy foods, such as testicles and cooked wheat, also poultry and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rottenness on the hide, but it hasn't reached the bone, cut away all the rotted part, and burn it with fire, then treat (the wound).
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein that does not stop bleeding without a bandage, and it cannot be staunched by medications, then seek the artery; and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if this does not help at all, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is easy:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and it is that you put in this powder which seals before the wound moves.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the way to make the powder is:
pren encens une partie;	Take incense one part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	Dragon's blood two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	Grind it finely and fill the wound, and bind it tightly until it adheres well and joins with all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	And then tie it securely, and leave it unbound unless it swells.
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Because one does not remove medicine until it is healthy again.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	"Sometimes this can also be done with quicklime alone when incense and dragon's blood are not available, but only if the air has not moved the wound."
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the wound has moved, especially in summer, do not apply this powder to it
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	Instead, apply some digested oils or poultices made from barley flour and water and honey until it softens
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with other treatments until it is healed
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a bone fracture accompanies the wound and it is small, remove it with fine forceps
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	I will tell you about head fractures later
de la plaie dou col	"Of the wound on the neck"
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	"If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one on the head, except when the nerve of the neck or an artery is cut."
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy than to leave them alone and not apply anything constricting, for they harm the nerves and cause them to retreat
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not apply anything cold to the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their connection is with the brain, which is the highest member
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	But let the medicine be warm, such as warm water mixed with honey and rose oil, and cooked in soft water, and other mineral stones according to this method, and moist poultices
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the wound is large, then stitch it up with thread and bind it with bandages until it heals."
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if wounds are deep and full of bowels, pierce it below or lower.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	If the artery is cut, and blood flows copiously, tie it off, ligate it, and cauterize it if necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	If the spine of the neck or heart is cut, and the vessels are preserved through which blood flows, then sew the heart to the windpipe, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then bind it tightly and leave it for a few days, then treat it with healing ointments until it is completely healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	If the wound has impressed upon the bone, scrape it away.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	If there are bone fragments, remove them all if you can; those that you cannot have, let the wound fester and drain, then ligate the opening.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wound is fresh, sprinkle it with the powder I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	"And if there are bones in the wound and there is a fistula, cure it as I have said in its chapter."
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	"Regarding wounds from spears or daggers,"
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a blow from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then observe whether wind enters the wound whenever the patient breathes.
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	you will know then that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep and the blood is fresh throughout, do not apply powder to it at first nor bind it tightly lest the blood retreat inwardly toward the heart and kill the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but apply an attractive ointment to it, binding it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you have no ointment, place old cotton in the wound to suck out moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	Otherwise, no spasm will come nor harmful trembling of the heart will occur;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good signs, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it with compresses and other treatments until it is healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	And if it cannot heal nor open, know that there is a fistula present.
si la cure si com on doit.	If the treatment is as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and is simple, or worse on the back, then treat that which is in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	If it is large, stitch it.
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	And if it is small, powder it, and if it is close to the bone and has cut pieces, then search the wound, and treat the edges if they are separated.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if they are not separated, then let the wound suppurate, so that the extraction will be easier.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	"Regarding rupture of the abdomen"
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the abdomen is great, medium, and small.
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	From a large wound sometimes the intestines or the nerve of the intestines leap out, which causes their intrusion.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	And stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one because it is harder to push the intestines back in unless they are put back piece by piece.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	Because the intestines swell quickly when they feel cold, drawing in more points, and therefore it is worth moving the wound, so that one can reset the intestines to their place along with the others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that there are four ways to perform an abdominal incision:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The two common sutures occur in the abdomen suture, and the suture of other wounds on the body has two more common sutures that are shared by other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	However, these sutures are most suitable for the abdomen, and I will describe each one and explain them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestines has been exposed, and there is no need for anything else, it should be done in one of two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	Moisten an sponge or the soft cloth in boiling water alone, or cook in water with vinegar and cumin and spices, and rinse the intestines until the swelling is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And sometimes doing this wine constricting, it is useful to wash wounds for reducing inflammation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling diminish, then moisten the intestines with water or ale and malt, for by this means the entrance is eased somewhat;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	And if it cannot enter, then make a small cut in the wound with the instrument used to tie off hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	And the first treatment is useful that the surgeon, that no one should cut without great necessity.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	And this is the instrument for splitting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	So cut inside in the curve and do not deviate, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines protrude outwards, then put them back according to their natural shape in their proper place, if you have the power, for this is useful.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide and it is in the lower part under the belly, then you must make the patient lie on their back and place their legs higher than their head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	And if it is in the lower abdomen part, raise the head and breast higher than the lower parts; similarly, if the intestine rupture is on one of the two sides, place attention so that the wounded part is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And thus you must arrange what I say for both large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	In small wounds, put on what you are equipped with, then place your hands gently around the wound and draw together its lips.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	And this is the common manner of suturing: take one or more needles according to the size of the wound's width, then leave two spaces from the wound's beginning, and insert a needle with good strong thread.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	And pierce the two ends of the skin with the two ends of the sinew which is beneath the skin inside, until you have pierced it on that side, and bring together the two ends of the sinew in four places.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then tie a doubled thread around the needle of two parts, then bring together the two heads of the wound gently, and then leave two spaces apart, and insert another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then tie the thread knot as you did with the first needle, and continue doing so according to how many needles you need until the entire wound is closed.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And let the needles be medium-sized, between fine and coarse; for too fine needles cut all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot enter properly.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	Therefore they must be of medium size.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	And do not push the needles too deep into the flesh and skin, lest they cut and reopen the wound before it can heal.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	Then cut the heads of the needles so they do not bother the patient while sleeping, and place small bandages or dressings on the needle heads to keep them in place until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	And this manner of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, where one or two needles suffice.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitch is common; you should bring together the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the flesh with one needle having a medium-strength thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	And once you have pierced these edges all together with the needle, then bring the needle back to the beginning of the stitch, in the manner one sews cloth.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	Space each stitch apart by the thickness of a barleycorn;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This stitch saves lives; I once sewed a wound in the belly of a man who was stabbed with a knife. The wound was over a palm's length wide and the bowels protruded by two palms' lengths.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I reset the intestines for him after he had been feverish for 24 hours, and the wound healed up to the 15th day, which I cleaned, and it was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physicians had judged that he would die, but it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	I did not treat him with ointments because there were none available in the place where I was.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	Apply cotton wool twice a day to the wound and rinse it with honey water until it is clean.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and insert it from the outer part to the inner one;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	When it has pierced the flesh straight through, then attach the head of the thread or the skin where you have inserted the needle, and make it pierce elsewhere from inside out;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And the purpose of this suture is that you should sew like a tanner sews leather, leaving the thread once on one side and taking it up again on the other until the entire suture is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second method of suturing, which Galen considers proper, is this: some people join the two parts naturally together and apply one end of the thread to the other in such a manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Stick a needle near the head of the liver, and pierce that spot alone, leaving both ends of the spleen untouched.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then twist the needle and make it pierce from the outer part inward toward the spleen's two heads.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then pierce both of them from the outer part inward toward the liver's two other heads that are on the opposite side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the usual way to cauterize and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	According to Galen, it is said that one should sew up the belly with two needles, each having thread on it.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one needle should be inserted from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who stitch hides.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Know that when the intestine is inside the belly, the stitching is more difficult than in other parts of the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of this wound is like the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	And it is necessary that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, before the art has moved it, then put back the intestine and sew up the cut.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	Then place powder around the flesh, and if the wound has moved, apply some ointment that is available, until the wound bows.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	And draw the thread tight, and let the lips of the wound be sewn together, and the skin.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat the wound like the others until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And if you do not have medicine, then apply old cotton as soon as the wound begins to ooze, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For in many cases where wounds are simple, no other medicine is needed;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And if you doubt that the wound will not communicate with the main limbs, it is necessary to wet light linen in warm oil of roses or rose oil, and place it around the angles and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	If he feels pain or corruption in his bowels, and this happens often, then perform black wine enemas. Moreover, if the corruption reaches the intestines,
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And if it pierces inside, know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines called "jejunum" cannot heal when wounded due to the thinness of their vessels and the delicacy of the entire body, as well as its similarity in nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	If the worm jumps out of the wound, push it back in like the intestines while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	And if it is old and has become worms or black, then tie the place that is black so that no blood flows there, because there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	Then cut what is between the tie, and put two heads of a knife dangling from the part below the wound until it reaches out to aid in extracting when the worms fall, and the wound opens.
de la routure dou boueil	from dislocation of the eyeball
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestines are torn, and the wound is small, it can sometimes be restored in some people; for example, I saw a man pierced in the belly with a spear,
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	And the wound was on the right side of the stomach, it was invaded and became a fistula, and excretion and wind escaped through it.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to probe until it was clean, and the area bound up.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him healed, I doubted that the patient might have some ailment in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	But there was no illness, he remained in better condition, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And some experts said that when one has a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	Take large leeches, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the leech has opened its mouth, place it on both lips so that it sucks there;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	And then cut off its head, and this holds so that it cannot detach itself, then place another leech afterward in the same manner as before, until the wound is entirely covered.
et cout la plaie.	and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If such a stone enters the intestines and causes no harm to the patient, then one can tie the intestines with a fine thread made from the gut of an animal, like this:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the head of this gut thread that is well scraped, and then tie at the head of this gut a thin twisted linen thread; then put the thread through the needle and stitch the intestine, and reset it in its place.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of sewing with threads is not used except according to the way of trust and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the small intestines, then there is no device nor health except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	"of fistula wherever it may be"
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know this: any wound or abscess that becomes hollow is universally called a 'fistula,' and likewise when it swells and contracts.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to truth a hard and white node that is not painful, and it is also shaped like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	And sometimes in clear jump bow, and other times thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	Sometimes small, and other times enough.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	And I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that any wound which is not clean and has no flesh, only appears as one of the nine causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	That is to say, by the smallness of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	Or because of its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	Or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips that does not allow flesh to grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	Or where there is too much bow.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	Or where the place is porous, and the matter is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	Or where the medicine used in the treatment is not good;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	Or because the corruption is a type of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	Or because the property in the region has delayed digestion and delayed healing, and is naturally inflamed.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	Or where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And I have already shown all these causes, signs, and medicinal remedies in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	"Now I must tell you about the treatment of fistula which is done by manual work."
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula occurs in all members of the body
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that come from large veins and arteries, and nerves, either in the face or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or near some of the ribs, or in the spinal cord of the back, or at any joint of the hands or feet
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and some come to the property of the main member and similar places
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas that are of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	And if there is any fistula that does not reach the place I have mentioned, and you are confident about its cure and recognize it, then take a tent of brass or iron, if the fistula is straight, and seek it
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	And if the fistula is twisted, search for it with a subtle tent of lead, for lead bends more around the twist
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	And if the fistula has many holes and you cannot search it well by touches, then cleanse it through one of the holes, for moisture flows quickly from one hole to another, and cleanses it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	Then search for blood as much as you can, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and how deep it is. Ask the patient well about the pain they feel when pressed by your hand, and where they feel it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	And once you truly know where it is, and if it's far from a joint, or nerve, artery, vein, or in any of the places I've told you, then cut according to what I've said. Remove the furthest layer and the rotten flesh that is inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	Then treat it until it is healed. And if the fistula is very deep in its proper place, then cut as deeply as you can. Then put moistened cloths soaked in hot water and vinegar at the mouth of the fistula until the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then I place compresses of healthy flesh until it is healed
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if it does not heal by this method, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If vein or nerve does not trouble you in the main limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, then wash until all corruption is removed, then dress with compresses of healthy flesh until it heals.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	And if it does not heal, and returns again as before, know that you have not yet reached the source:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	So uncover and search until you reach the bottom, remove all corruption, then replace it in its proper place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if it is healed thus, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep to reach.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	So there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	And if there is a small broken bone, and you can grasp it with tongs, then remove it using the appropriate tool; but if there are many bones, pull them all out together, leaving none behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	And if moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, then cut away the moisture and flesh, and expose the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then place something irritating to corruption on the wound, and let it remain until the surrounding flesh is corrupted; and then the bones will come out more easily.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	And if it's a large bone, like those of the leg or thigh, then remove only the corruption until all the blackness is gone; then dress the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	And if there is much corruption, and it reaches even to the bone,
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	So it must be cut away entirely down to the corruption, then treated until it heals solid.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And I will tell you of a fistula which happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	A young man of about 30 years suffered pain in his leg due to an internal cause that brought matter into the limb, causing a large swelling without apparent reason for opening.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	Yet the physicians, through their foolishness, operated so much on the swelling that it opened, and there flowed out much matter, becoming a fistula with many openings that poured forth wind and moisture from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	And many physicians tried to treat it for about two years, but none were skilled in the art of hands, so I was called and saw his leg and the remedies with which they had treated him, and what flowed out through the openings was great.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And the young man's body became red, and he had a yellowish hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then sought all the holes, and found that one came against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I therefore hurried and cut into one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, which was decayed and perforated, and corruption had reached the bone within.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I saw what appeared to me of the decayed bone, and thought that there was no other decay besides that which I removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	And I began to heal the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but it would not close.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	Then I began again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found that the decay had continued in the bone, which I scraped out, and then removed it, and tried to close the space.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	But even so, I could not close more than half a palm's width of the bone, and scraped it away entirely, then restored it with medicines.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	And it was soon healed and closed, but there was still no need to resume the operation except for the weakness of the patient who could not endure it, and out of fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because often blood was evacuated, but he became entirely healthy, and in place of the bone, hard flesh grew, and it was of good condition and had no harm or opposite at all, neither in going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take the lien, and stretch it over the head of the bone that opens, and command him to extend it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	And place another lien of thick linen over the first lien, and tie it above the flesh that is over the bone; stretch the head so that you pull out the corrupted flesh below, and uncover the flesh on the spot where you wish to perform the cautery, so that the heat does not blister the flesh.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	And place a truss or a spoon underneath the bone to move away the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And it should be done until one can see and feel the corruption, and then once again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or on one side; uncover all the flesh.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	Then place a truss underneath, and then cauterize from one side of the corruption to the other; the length of the cautery should be equal to the length of the corruption as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if corruption is in the joint, cut off the corrupted joint, even the bone that contains it on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if corruption is between two joints, there is no other option but to cut.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	And if corruption is at the wrist of the hand or foot, it is very serious, but nonetheless you must examine this corruption and how it appears.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	And cleanse it in every way that you can, but avoid cutting veins or nerves.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And know that the blades and saws for cutting these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and fineness, and their length and shortness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And therefore one must prepare an appropriate tool for each type of operation.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And know that the work will show you which tool you need, according to your knowledge of this art and the evidence of the disease's nature;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If you consider the instrument with which you have need according to what is necessary.
dou feu	"from fire"
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head rots either due to an internal cause or a lack of force;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	And when you have treated that corruption with medicines but they do not help, then it is necessary to cut off the limb up to where the corruption reaches so that the patient escapes death or the greater harm of the loss of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	And the sign is that the limb becomes black as if burned by fire, and afterwards the corruption spreads from limb to limb, and then it takes over the whole body;
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	So hurry to cut off, and if it is due to the sting of venomous beasts like the sea scorpion or snake etc., if the corruption reaches the elbow joint then cut it off but do not allow it to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes to the hand, cut it at the joint so that the corruption does not come to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	And if it comes to the arm, then cut at the elbow;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	And if it passes the elbow, it's death, and there is no benefit in applying external remedies however great their virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	And likewise when corruption comes to the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	If it comes to the first joint, cut after the next joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, cut off the whole foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it ascends into the leg, cut at the knee joint
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it reaches above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And the manner of cutting off or cauterizing the limb is thus: you tie it above and below, and stretch one servant downwards from one tie, and another upwards from the other tie; and cut open the flesh that lies between the two ties with a broad spatula until the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Then cut or cauterize it, and place a linen cloth on each side so that the cautery does not touch the healthy flesh, and the patient receives no other injury or abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if bleeding begins when you operate, then cauterize the location promptly, where you apply some constricting powders.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your treatment until it is completed, then bind the wounded limb with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	And I shall tell you what happened in Rome once:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	A blackness appeared on him that seemed burned by fire, and this corruption first came upon his right foot, spreading to consume the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the man saw the corruption, he quickly covered his foot, and it was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And many years later the corruption returned to his left hand, and he came to me; after cleansing his body I applied caustic substances, but still the corrosion could not stop.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	And it seemed that I should cut off his hand, but I did not want to do so, having hope that we might drive out the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	And I also doubted whether if I cut his hand he would die, for the virtue of the man was weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	And he despaired entirely and returned to his land, and hastened to have his hand amputated, and he became healthy.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I only recount this so that others may know how to act if such need arises.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess forms in the flesh and stays so long that it collects a great mass of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then it becomes red and bursts open, and the pus jumps out, and the spot remains empty like an empty vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And the skin above it is as thin as stretched fabric, and it does not extend to the bone or the nerve, and such a disease is called "sound," and is not called "fistula.
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if it extends so far that it reaches the bone deeply, then it is called a "fistula
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And it is fitting for you to cut that skin all around, especially if it is thin, just like a piece of cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and let it not be worried about its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you believe that the skin may decay and corruption is not deep, but the skin is thick with flesh, then perform a clyster thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	look if the breast is large and the belly that it enters has a foul odor, then perform a clyster with Egyptian medicine made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take equal amounts of aloe and oil, and litharge, and cook them together in a vessel over the fire until the medicine becomes red and thick like honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And then take as much of it as you need, and mix it with water or honey, and administer it through a clyster, closing the hole tightly.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine remain there for two hours, then remove it by squeezing gently.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this many times until the breast is bandaged and the pus is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and sometimes you should use a warm water enema made from vine ash, especially when this medicine is not present; you should take ashes of burnt grapevine wood and pour boiling water over them, then sift it and use it as an enema until you know that the breast is well cleansed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	And if the patient cannot tolerate it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water made from ashes, then use a warm water and honey enema with a bit of powdered lead.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	Or you can use an enema made from honey and mixed wine, so that the honey has properties to cleanse and wash, and the wine makes the blood thin.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And once you have done this and you are confident that the breast is well cleansed, then use an enema made from a substance that causes flesh to grow there; take diaphoretic plaster and mix it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	When you apply the enema of certain medications and ointments, whose properties I have mentioned when discussing ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And if the opening of the anus is small and the tube of the enema cannot enter it, then widen it a little with an iron tool, and insert a wick of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is widened enough.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the wound is too wide, then leave only enough skin to allow the enema tube to enter, and if the opening of the bowels that excrete faces is above, cut it lower or at its current level.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the intestines are deep within, leave flesh behind there.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot reach the bottom of the wound as you wish, then prepare it in such a way that the intestines lie at their lowest point, for when the intestines are deep within, leave flesh behind there. And if you cannot reach the bottom of the wound as you wish
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	If the bow moves too easily downward, do not leave anything on the bowstring.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	Take medicines that solidify to apply on the skin, and press them with a linen cloth covering the whole wound;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	Then cut as deeply as possible around the hole in the skin about an inch wide; then apply a gentle ointment on another cloth according to the size of the wound, and place it on the wound to relieve the bowstring's tension. Do not remove the outer large cloth until after many days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	The one on the wound's hole should often remove it to remove the bowstring, and know what flows from the bowstring whether it is venomous or little or much, digested or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	And watch out if the patient feels pain or numbness, and if there is an abscess or not. When your medicine has spread in this way and you see what comes out of the wound's hole, then know that the chest is already healed, and approach the healing.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	And then you loosen it in the morning or on the third day, and when you open the wound, change the other bandage and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if after many days the breast continues to secrete undigested milk, know that the breast is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons come after a long time, do not despair of health, for recovery is near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are people whose wounds heal slowly with flesh, and others who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if undigested food jumps from the stomach after many days, know that the stomach is not empty;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	And if the stomach is slow to empty and is distant, apply drying medicines in substance and power, such as diaphoretic ointments, for there is much vitriol in them, and this is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take diaphoretic ointment, and it is made with rose oil, and rose petals equal in weight;
puis le confit et en use;	Then mix it together and use it.
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	And if diaphoretic ointment is not present, you can also make it better by cooking honey and increasing its size, or take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them, and powder them onto the honey while it is on the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	And then apply a bandage made of drapery; let it lie upon the breast, and sometimes administer a long aristolochia, and roots of blue lily, which is also like flour of barley and centory.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	And in using simples or compounds:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	Grind them and make powder, and put upon the honey that I have mentioned, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	And if the wound is prolonged, and not healed by this treatment, know that corruption has gone deep, causing impression on the bone, or in hard members, or in ligaments.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	If it is the cure for a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the boil of the toe
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the little finger of the hand or foot, or sometimes arises in other toes.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	And when it is elderly and not cared for, then a hot abscess comes, and they run and tear so much that they reach the root of the nail, sometimes tearing it all.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Rust spreads to the bone, causing foul-smelling pain; the skin becomes doubly wide, and turns yellowish.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	If you treat it as we have said in the section above and yet the treatment does not help, then you must cut away with iron all the excess that remains of the nail, after which cauterize the wound.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is greatly beneficial if the bone is healthy, and the nail is sound;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	And if the nail presses into the flesh and begins to prick and cause a blister, you must place the point of a knife under the nail that is piercing the flesh, lift it up, and carefully scrape away the affected skin, then apply burning and corrosive medicines to the remaining flesh to remove all [of the affliction].
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply dressings until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	If the corruption has reached the bone, cut it away and burn it out, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, healing cannot occur;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you see that both [joints] are corrupting, cut them off with a knife as was mentioned earlier, then treat them until they are healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	If he is struck, bruised, and feels great pain, then you must clean it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the nail of the big toe in a crosswise direction and make sure that the cut does not reach the flesh underneath the nail, as this would cause great pain to the patient;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, then put something on it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of gout in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Some people are sometimes born with both hands completely fleshy, and sometimes there is bone in them, and sometimes there is a nail, and some are born at the root of the joint, where the birth is in certain fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those born with a bent little toe do not move, and those born at the joint of the little toe may move occasionally;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The cut in those that are fleshy is easy, as follows:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it off at its root with a broad knife.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	Those born at the root of the joint are difficult to treat;
si te tien dou coper.	So hold while cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In one who is born deaf or becomes deaf later on, you should first cut the flesh around the bone all the way to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, and then polish it until it is smooth.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sinews that come together at the two joints come by birth, or by the union of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You must cut off that swelling so that the little toes return to their natural shape;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two bandages or moistened cloths soaked in rose oil so they do not swell again;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Place two thin pieces of lead between them until the joint is soundly fixed.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling occurs on either side with the palm, scrape away this scurf as needed.
des vils	(of villains)
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The veins are large, engorged tubes full of melancholic impurities that come from various parts of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And this happens more often in legs of those who walk and work and carry things than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you should administer to him a laxative for the colon, and then the holy water of the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	There are two ways to perform the iron cure:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One is by pricking it with a cautery and drawing out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The other way is to raise the vein and draw all of its blood.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The incision should be made in this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	First, wash the leg with hot water very thoroughly until the thick blood is thinned out, then press the leg of the patient from above the hip down to just below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then make one incision in the vein where it is most prominent, using a wide cut, then squeeze and draw out as much of the black blood by hand from one end to the other until the patient can no longer tolerate it;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then the ulcer, command him to anoint with fats from the innards of a black pig;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And recommence evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, harming the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The raising of him is in this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Rise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then place it in a bath, and raise the leg with warm water until it becomes red, and the veins swell;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, heat it by fire, and then cut at the vein near the long tendon at the top of the knee, or in the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin with an awl, and strip the vein from each side until it becomes visible when touched;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it appears like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	Then place the tweezers beneath it until it is lifted from the skin, and then cut it lightly with an awl, then cut in another place three inches further.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it up with a razor, as you have done, and press it onto another sinew, as you had done first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then cut another incision, or several if needed, then lift it and cut at the two sides of the foot, then draw it out and lift up to the second incision.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then extract it from incision to incision until it all comes out, then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot draw it out and lift it, then insert a needle with strong doubled thread, tie it and draw it out, place it under the skin, and twist your hand back and forth until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And make sure it doesn't cut, because if it cuts, you cannot draw it out or lift it, which causes harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	And when you have completely treated it, then place wet wool soaked in wine and rose oil over the wound site;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep treating him until he is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	If the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped around itself, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not sever it completely.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron tool used to cut a vein is curved, and it does not sever the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And its curve should be large, because if it were thin, it would cut into the vein; but it should be thick as we have said. Here is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein runs through the legs, in warm regions where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry land with no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	And sometimes it may appear elsewhere than on the legs, such as when rot occurs under the skin, like how worms and leeches move between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is that there comes a very great inflammation in the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to protrude outward like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the vein opens, you must wrap a piece of lead around it, from one and a half to two fingers wide, and tie it; leave the lead hanging on the leg. Every time blood flows out, wrap the lead around it and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut off a portion of it, wrap up the remaining part, but do not cut it at its root so that it remains intact.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cut it, it will enter into the flesh and cause an abscess and rottenness in that place, and evil disease;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	So therefore it must be treated little by little until its end, and nothing of it should remain on the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And sometimes this vein can be treated with the palms of the hands, measuring 12 or 18 inches, and a man once came to me whose had measured 18 inches long; but when you cut it, insert an iron rod into its opening, pierce it right through until all is out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And let the matter that is inside be emptied, and apply healing medicines at the place every few days, then treat it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes this vein has many branches, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or in the foot, and there are many openings from which blood flows;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Treat it then as we have said earlier.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land 'cattle disease', because it often happens to oxen, and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, which travels throughout the body moving up and down; one feels it well when it goes from limb to limb, until it reaches the skin where it goes, and leaves behind.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And is caused by putrefaction of certain humours, such as worms, serpents, and roundworms and ascarids in the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	And there is doubt about its severity, for when it travels through the body and reaches the head, sometimes it enters the eye and destroys it.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	This happens frequently.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being treated or pulled out, one can only do so when it is moving:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	Therefore, tie the place above and below with a strong, tight bandage, then cut it open and pull out the worm; if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh and you cannot find it, cauterize the area with fire until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm that it causes is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said.
