et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it coming near the head of the eye, press down firmly under the eyebrow, then cut across, and cauterize.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And the patient should use cleansing of body with dissolving medicines for harmful humors, and avoid eating rotten foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From pain caused by windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This illness is called in our land 'vakkhir', and it is a pain that comes to certain limbs, which then moves from limb to limb;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	And shortly afterward, it moved like a worm up to the shoulder faster than anything else, just as quicksilver moves from one place to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain then left that spot and lodged in the shoulder, and afterward it quickly spread throughout the body until it reached the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then she told me that she would turn around again around her body as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	"I was greatly amazed at how she moved from limb to limb in this way, for I had never seen this disease manifest itself like this before."
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I had wanted many times before that she might want to move from one place to another without pain, but I had not seen this in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body and visible veins, and therefore this constrained windiness appeared;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and there is no apparent reason for this in those who are delicate and have moist bodies and concealed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see this disease being cured, and the patient feels that pain which we have described, then quickly apply plaster above and below it, and then cut until that constrained windiness escapes its place;
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the location;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	If you do not see it with your own eyes, then treat it with remedies that expel windiness, such as fetid pills and pills of senna, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	"The causes of hiccups are varied according to their appearances and the parts of the body where they occur."
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The varieties of them are such that there are those which have large points, and small ones, hairy and smooth.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And there are some with two angles, others with lengths, and still others in fragments.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	And those that fall onto any limb do so in one of two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Either it falls on principal limbs, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls into any location on these limbs, the signs of death that I will tell you about appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	So you should beware of extracting this arrow, for afterwards many deaths occur.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And if this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not embedded deeply, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of an arrow striking the brain is when it pierces the bone and bursts the fontanelle above the brain; this includes sudden and severe headache, dimming of vision with redness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms, loss of consciousness, vomiting of bile,
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	And perhaps without force from the nostrils, or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And perhaps loses speech and voice
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And there may be moist white discharge like poultry's blood, which also burns like raw flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	Should this sign appear to you, take care, and remove the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of an arrow hitting the heart are that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And perhaps the arrow moves like poultry, and black blood comes out, accompanied by coldness and cold sweat, and fainting;
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Then you may be sure that the man will die.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	"The sign of hiccups that occur near the lung is when foamless sputum suddenly comes from the wound; the throat swells up and the patient changes color, sighs loudly, and seeks cold air."
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow hits the lung's covering, it is near the ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and causes great pain and sorrowful sighing;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and all the shoulder joints move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	"And if hiccups occur in the stomach, sometimes undigested meat comes out from the wound."
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	"And if hiccups occur in the belly and blood flows through the intestines suddenly, there is no hope of recovery or extraction of the hiccup."
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow hits the bladder, urine comes out and there is defecation, and the patient feels intense pain;
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Know that wounds are deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	"Other limbs, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, auxiliary muscles, spinal column, buttocks, thighs, and legs, etc., are safe according to many conditions."
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	"When hiccups occur in a nerve or artery and are not venomous, as I will tell you happened to me so that you may do the same."
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened at a man's house where an arrow fell into the root of his nose
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and drew it out on the other side under the ear's fat without causing harm
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And at another time I drew out an arrow that had fallen into the fat of the eye under its lid, and the arrow was barbed so that only its tip could be reached towards the wood, and it was large like a Turkish bow, all iron light without ears;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The wound healed without any bad consequences.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And drew out an arrow from the throat of a Christian; the arrow was Arab, with ears;
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I cut the barbs and teased it out until I drew it out, and the Christian healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And drew out an arrow from a man who had fallen into his belly, thinking that he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	And then, after passing thirty days, his condition did not change.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut on the arrow, pierced it, and pulled it out with fire; there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man onto whom an arrow has fallen on his back, and the wound is closed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remained within him, and did not change its natural state nor cause harm to any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man onto whom an arrow fell on his face, and the wound was closed;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and remained thus without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	And many others like this.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And pulled out an arrow from the neck of one of the king's servants, which had fallen into his throat and was slightly leaning towards the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was entirely buried.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called for treatment three days after it had fallen.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I sought it with all subtlety and did not feel it at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pain and pressure under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was the tip of the arrow I placed a comforting plaster with digestive properties because the wound did not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and then I saw the point of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the plaster again each day and the wound healed over. The patient felt the arrowhead on the ninth day.
et il le me dist.	And he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound daily until it opened. I tested and felt the tip of the arrowhead which was bent.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I inserted a probe into the wound's opening with that corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow became clearly visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And this lasted about four months. Then the wound became swollen so that I could not insert the forceps and pull out the arrowhead.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Therefore, I did not cease to devise and contrive methods of instruments until on the tenth day I obtained good tongs according to what its shape will come to in the end of this chapter, so that I pulled it and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physicians judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I then restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient became entirely healthy.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Now I have told you about the extraction of certain arrows; therefore, set your care upon what I have not said, for books cannot encompass everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Yet the wise master compares even small things and finds new works and nine instruments for the treatment of unusual cases that arise in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows enter the limbs where they are struck in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either at the point where they enter, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And that which jumps forward where it enters is an arrow entering flesh, and sometimes it jumps suddenly.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump now, let it remain until the flesh can be pulled around it, and the joint relieved.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, let it remain for some days, and move it each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will jump out, and if it does not, carefully cut around the entire point with a fine blade until the surrounding area is widened, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the bone of the head and goes into one of the ventricles of the brain, some of the accidents that I have mentioned may befall the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	do not pull it out but leave it alone for some days until it is even with the surface again, because if the arrowhead comes into the brain, death will follow.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrowhead is stuck only in the bone and does not reach the brain, and the patient remains for some days without bad symptoms, then you can attempt to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is deeply stuck thus and cannot come out, then apply poultices around it as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the place until it is sound.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrowhead is stuck in such a way that one cannot see it, then search for it everywhere.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, then draw it out with some tool.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrowhead, and there is neither bone nor nerve nor vein, then make it wider until the wound is large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	And draw out the arrowhead if you can, and if it has ears by which it holds, then remove the flesh that is stuck into it on both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrowhead so that you can draw it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And be careful not to break the arrowhead while drawing it out, for this would cause greater pain.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	"And if you cannot do it all at once, leave the arrowhead until the wound around it is healed, then pull it out, for extraction will be easier."
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding is contrary to you, then follow what we have said about its treatment in this chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	And guard against incising the nerve or the vein; and devise how you can carefully remove the arrowhead without danger, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and place the patient in the position they were in when the arrow struck them, for that is the greatest help. And if you cannot do this, then place them according to the signs that indicate it.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	An arrow that comes from another side, where something of it is visible or the skin is swollen there, can be felt around it:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	then cut down until forceps can grasp it, and then extract it.
si saut fuer maintenant.	If it is stuck now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, twist your hand round until it enters the bone and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now and then resume the extraction until it comes out:
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is a splinter of the arrowhead, remove the entire piece.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	And if the stake falls, and you wish to administer cautery, then insert the heated instrument so that the tip of the arrow enters the wound of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	Then apply fire, and if the arrow is stuck in deep, insert the heated instrument with its point entering inside to ease extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrowhead has touched the lung,
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls into the thigh, belly, bladder, ribs or side, and it is near, and you can reach it, then cut towards it;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut the vein or nerve, then extract it, and then stitch the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat splints is similar to a bird's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	There are many ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	Large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like that of a bird's feather, for striking at the tip of the arrow, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the pliers for attaching and removing is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common flesh
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are 31 veins from which bloodletting is performed, among them there are 16 that are located in the head, namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	The two temporal veins behind the ears, called the 'doubles' or 'twin' veins;
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	And the two arteries that are visible in both temples.
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And the two veins that are in the inner corners of both eyes, which are called 'aspires'.
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is within the forehead.
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	And the vein that is at the back of the neck.
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	And the two glands that are in the neck.
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are above the lips of the mouth, which are called 'auguerich'.
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins commonly spoken about are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	The first is the cephalic, and it runs along the right side of the chest, which common people call 'the vein of the head'.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	And the second is called 'fast', and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilica veins; common people call this 'the vein of the heart'.
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And the basilica runs along the left side of the chest; common people call it 'the vein of the belly', and it is above the forearm; this is the one that is openly visible in the elbow pit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the savatelet is the vein which is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	And in the leg and at the foot are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	the first is under the curve of the pocket on the left side, and the second is the saphenous vein which is at the ankle on the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein called "nisse," which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And under those are three veins in the other leg.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of veins that are behind the ears helps with ancient catarrhs and headaches.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	And the qualities of bleeding are such that you should raise the patient's head and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth.
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	Then have the patient strain his neck with a vise until two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	So grasp them with your fingers and where you feel the pulse beneath your fingers, then squeeze tightly;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lancet and insert it under the vein up to the bone, then raise your hand along the entire length of the vein, and cut through the skin and vein firmly twice near the crossing point, allowing blood to flow until you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then squeeze it and bind it tightly until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already discussed incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The surgery of the two arteries that are in the two temples is useful for migraine, headache, and customary ophthalmia, and for the course of tears from the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the qualities of the surgeon are as I said
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	And it is that the patient stretches out their neck so that both veins appear clearly.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And feel the pulse beneath your thumb, and then press firmly
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then place your fingertip on the vein above your thumb, insert the lancet underneath it, raise the vein up and cut it as you did with the other veins, allowing blood to flow according to your needs.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then remove from the patient and place your two hands on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on top.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And then tie it firmly, leaving it until it is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And we have spoken of their causes and remedies, at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the frontal vein is as good as that of the temporal vein for treating old facial diseases, migraine, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality is such that the patient strains their neck by twisting it, until the veins appear;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called the 'fossor', of which this is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein and press with your hand or something else, allowing blood to flow out according to what you desire.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then untie the patient's neck and tie the vein until it is healed, often using a wide bandage.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, the bandage should not be too tight;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	And move it across, for the bone is near, and sometimes the ligaments break when they are thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The cautery of the two veins that are in the temples helps against eyestrain, and against headache, and against redness, and against the whiteness in the eye, and against facial diseases.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the qualities of its cautery are such that the patient twists his neck to one side, as previously mentioned.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then the cautery, and let the cautery be across, somewhat long, somewhat wide with fire, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the fire is too thin, it might break.
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then let blood flow freely until you have enough, and then bind with cotton, binding it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The cautery of the vein on the neck is good for ague, and for manic frenzy, and for facial diseases, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, especially when it is chronic.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	The quality of sneezing is that the patient strains their neck, then holds their nose to your left hand, and takes a long thin reed and sticks it between the two nostrils in the space that is not open well, and now blood will begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not go too deep, make the blood flow according to your need, then let it lie for one night, for it will be quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	This is the shape of the reed:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	Sneezing from both nostrils helps with childbirth, the beginning of menstruation, and many diseases, including measles, scabies, and hernias.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of sneezing is that the patient strains their neck on both sides, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	And let the master stand on the patient's head, and the patient sit on a seat, then open the vein with a long cut slightly wide, then draw out blood temperately or as much as needed.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then perform another on the other vein, then untie it, and gently compress around the veins so that the patient does not strangle.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let it be until morning, for the wound to heal.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The sanctity of the veins above the lips helps with coughing in the mouth and with gum corrosion, lip fissures, nosebleeds, and around the nostrils
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of healing are such that you should make the patient sit before you, and hold their neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip and look at two veins, one on the right side of the lip and the other on the left, which are known by their black color and by the small black veins around them;
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	therefore cut one and the other, but if you do not recognize them or are in doubt, then cut the largest of each side, and similarly do for the two veins above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the health beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The healing of the veins below the tongue helps after the healing of the temporal vein, and it is for the tightening of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the qualities of the pulse are that the patient feels between your hands before the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks down on each side for a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then feel both, but do not go too deep, as underneath are the arteries
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the wrist that are commonly felt are felt in two ways
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either pricking like a broad flame, or olive-like and subtle like a cutting edge, and is called "anesis";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	And they are broad or subtle according to the width and narrowing of the veins
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the myrtle flame is very well-known, and it is wide as you see
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	It is necessary to open hairless veins filled with visible thick blood that contain thick and turbid blood
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive-like flame
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more finely pointed and is for healing thin veins that contain clear yellow blood
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The pulse of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps those with illnesses below the throat, neck, breast, and belly
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And the pulsator must feel for rigor and beware of the artery underneath
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he severs the artery, and blood begins to flow, it must be staunched, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And the flame should not be sharp, but cutting like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilisk does not open plainly, you must remove it and replace with another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you want any part of it, or you sew in its place the vein within the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	It opens plainly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And cut with a knife-like flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see the location of the vein, then you should also remove the arm, and touch the location until you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the point from below, then tie the arm, and cut the vein with a knife-like flame;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	And beware that you do not strike the artery when you see the location swollen, for it is the artery:
eschui la donques.	Squeeze it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see something red and thin like a child's urine coming out on top, know that it is arterial blood:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and place your thumb firmly upon it; then remove your thumb if the bleeding stops, for this happens many times.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	Bind up the arm, leave it thus, and do not let the patient move it
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be afraid to move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the bleeding does not stop and you faint, and a physician is not present, then cut the artery if it is visible, for its mouth will contract.
et estainche li sans.	and the bleeding will cease.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a bark of fig and cut it open, then take one half and bind it securely until the next day
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if the bleeding has stopped, that's good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	But if not, then treat it with powders that stop blood flow, as we have said
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stitching is not considered sufficient in many cases due to the smallness of the wound's opening, and the power of the sinews of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The vein in the middle if it stands out helps to draw blood from above the head and below the body, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and the surgeon must be careful for the nerve that is beneath, and if it goes too deep and touches the nerve, and swells, the wound will not heal properly, and sometimes it cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve often opens, and if it does not open in some people due to its fineness, then you must cauterize it with the instrument called 'anesil'.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And avoid touching the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is space between the two nerves, make an incision along it
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The cephalic vein also helps to draw blood from the head and aids the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to cauterize with the olive-oil flame or the myrtle flame, for it is the safest of all veins, as there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, it is necessary to find the lightest place, and do not give up if it fails the first time; start again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and sometimes the place swells in some people when it fails the first time, but it causes no harm
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the surgery depends on your skill.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about cauterization is that it is only performed to maintain health and prevent future illnesses
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the cautery be made on one of the three veins located at the elbow:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	namely, the cephalic, basilica, and forearm veins
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and cauterization should be performed at the beginning of Lent, in autumn, and in winter after meals, when the sign of repletion appears.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and cauterization should be done on the first or third day, after two or three hours into the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The medicine administered to patients has no fixed time, but whenever there is need by day or night, at all hours and at any time;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Nor should children be given medicine until they are fourteen years old, nor women during the first four months of pregnancy until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should one operate on the elderly who have passed sixty years of age
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when anyone wishes to take medicine in any manner, it is necessary that they cleanse the intestines with a light enema if there is much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw harmful impurities from the intestines into the main organs.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor should one take medicine who is too full of food, nor one who is drunk, until they sober up, nor one who is dropsical.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And beware of taking medicine after an attack of the colic, vomiting, diarrhea, excessive menstruation in women, hard labor, wakefulness and fasting, or any great weakness, either from illness or injury to the body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then refine the humors if blood is thick, by foods and beverages and medicines, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	Then use a bath, if nothing prevents it, to refine the blood, and wash the vein around the third rib, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And guard yourself that day from work, and overeating, and lust, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	And be at ease and joyful, and let the vein being bled be higher than the others, and rub the arm twice or thrice, then tie the bandage moderately, for if it is too tight or loose, blood cannot flow correctly.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	Then rub the place with both hands until the veins swell and can be felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Then wet the vein with a little bit of old oil, then place his left thumb on the vein below where he intends to bleed, ensuring that the vein does not bulge or break when struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flee as if they were strings in the skin, and some of these are filled with windiness so that when one applies fire, it retreats from the fire and cannot open the vein; and thus some people are.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, for which reason the surgeon should be careful in such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens on the first attempt, that's good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, then start again a little lower or higher suddenly, if the area is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the area is swollen and the patient is afraid, let him wait one or two days without binding his arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	perhaps a boil will appear;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Do not enter into baths, then continue the cautery if he wishes.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the hole is small and blood flows subtly, or you doubt that enough blood is flowing, then apply fire directly to that hole with all force.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	And perform it rather hastily, before the place becomes inflamed.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	For this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place inflamed, do not recommence the cautery, but put on a little oil ointment, for it lightens the body of blood and turns the inflammation to the better in this place.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And apply the ointment of oil in every cautery you perform on veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	This same thing does tripcord and bowstring when applied to the place.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	So that the blood is thinned out and dispersed when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there appears a large abscess, which often happens, especially when no cautery was performed except at the time when the vein was opened and the opening was small, then hasten to apply an sponge moistened in hot water and salt, and compress it for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And it is necessary that you do this after the flow of blood from the vein stops, and if any blackness or greenness remains in place after some days, then it does no harm;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see, place something of aloe or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, mastich, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times an abscess and swelling appear at the site of the incision:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Then place your hand on it, and if you find the spot soft under pressure from your hand, then that appearance is harmful.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	So be careful not to place anything of what we have said there, for fear of damaging the artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	But make a dry poultice to harden the spot, then treat it with another cure until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw off blood according to its quantity and according to its color.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	And if you see it thick, let it be until it thins;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	And if he is too hot, let him cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	It is necessary for one who is full and fat, and needs bloodletting, that a larger incision be made, and the flame be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	But for one who is weak, do the opposite; they must be bled more gently and frequently, and bleeding should be done by cutting across rather than pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bloodletting prevents loss of blood and injury to nerves, and is better than bleeding done with a long or wide instrument.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	For one whose body fails at being bled, it is necessary to give them a drink made from crushed pomegranate juice.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If they are overheated, let them bleed three or four times; but if they have a cold complexion, let them drink beforehand a decoction made from musk syrup or honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chicory, well scented.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after losing much blood, afterwards he should inhale broth of flesh, and fragrant subtile syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the chapter on syncope for evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to empty the arm vein and be bled again later, it is necessary that when he is weakened by much bloodletting, he be bled little by little according to his continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to empty the arm vein after the first bloodletting and has a strong body, should be bled seven hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to have blood drawn from another vein should be bled on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood within the body which has already become heated, causing fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	If it becomes necessary to draw out a large quantity of blood, then one should widen the incision as far as it falls into palm
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	Then, after dressing all the wounds and placing your hand on the pulsating flesh when it heals, ensure that nothing comes in place of palm, for this often happens when healers are careless;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And do not, when you see a loosened arm and blood begins to flow for the second time, close the wound without pressing firmly upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	Nor if it is curved, should he hastily extend his arm, for this would be harmful;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	But allow him to remain until it heals a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Where you should touch with the tip of fire until the blood that has frozen at the mouth of the vein flows out again, and put on some cotton wool moistened in water, pressing lightly upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not squeeze it until the inflammation has subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is a necessity to draw blood a second time, do so in the same vein or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are bled in place of the head vein because they are connected.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of the healing is thus: The patient places their hand in warm water until the bones are red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then it should be bound moderately, so that the vein appears clearly; then apply the cautery across, not along or lengthwise.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And the hole should be wide; cauterize it close to the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot flow out, put the hand back in warm water until enough blood has flowed into the water.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it's wintertime, do not put the hand back in hot water, for one puts it in more often in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And cauterizing this vein is safer than any other, as there are no arteries or nerves there.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The cautery of the vein on the right hand [palm] is beneficial for all diseases of the liver; this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Press the hand and put it in warm water until the vein swells so that it can be seen;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the sinew is transverse, and you cut it entirely throughout, then it causes no harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	And do not cut too deeply, for nerves lie beneath all sinews of flesh; then place the hand in warm water if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot flow out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	"And once you have cleaned off as much blood as necessary, then place a bandage of oil and flax to quickly bind the wound, and do this for each wound."
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	"The swelling in the left hand is attributed to mouse disease, so perform the same treatment as I have instructed for the right hand."
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve of the spleen is beneficial for all ailments beneath the body, such as diseases of the marrow, retention of fluids, diseases of the reins, and old afflictions of the thighs and legs, and similar ailments.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the procedure for this dislocation is that the patient places his foot in warm water and rubs along the vein until it breaks, then tie above the ankle joint.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	The vein is at the ankle, and many veins go up the leg from there.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Therefore cut where the largest vein runs, or at the ankle.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you cut on the leg, beware of the nerves beneath and also cut transversely as in cutting sinews.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the blood flow out freely.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	"And if the blood cannot flow out, then put the foot back in the water and allow the vein to drain well."
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the first incision fails, then begin again a little higher up because the place is salted.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not hesitate on nerve, as we have said, and likewise do so with the sinew of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	"The location of the sciatic vein is at the outer ankle joint, and its cauterization benefits sciatica pain when it is due to hot blood."
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of its heating is that when the patient enters the bath, he should strain on top of the ankle four times while twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, then heat in all ways that you can, and crosswise;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is important that you cover it quickly, for the place is bare, and it responds much to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	But if you do not find it, then heat any vein that opens on the back of the foot, towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and do so until you see blood flow, then untie the bandage, and put cotton on it and bind it.
ele est maintenant sanee.	It is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	And regarding cupping treatments
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Ventouses are made of horns, or earthenware, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And bloodletting is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Wherever you strike and draw blood.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this cauterization without striking is of two kinds:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is performed with fire or without fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	And cauterization done by striking and drawing blood is performed on fourteen parts of the body, one of which is located on top of the head.
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the other is in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	And two others are on either side of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And the cupping glass below the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	And the cupping glasses for both shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the cupping glasses for the elbows;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the cupping glasses for both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	And the cupping glasses for both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	And the cupping glasses for both ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and cauterization without bloodletting treats only the small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and does not weaken the body in any way.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered with or without fire in any disease caused by excess until the entire body has been evacuated.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if it is necessary to undergo bloodletting due to illness or custom, let us perform it each hour at the beginning of the month or at the end, and also in between every time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are some who, when they need bloodletting, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And others find fulfillment and redness in their face, and in their head, and on the neck, and darkness before the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	Others experience a taste of blood in their mouth, have an swollen tongue, and cough up blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And there are those who dream or see blood flowing, wounds, death, or similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	"And when we see these signs, especially if they occur during the month, we order cupping to be performed after three hours of the day."
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The sweat of the face helps against the headache that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary for this to happen after evacuating everything from the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And this bloodletting takes the place of sweating from the head, and those who are of cold temperament or have a cough should not practice it, for it causes them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And therefore, it is not necessary for the elderly to use them, nor those with cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	"And those who often bleed themselves become forgetful, so one must place the cupping vessel a little lower down to avoid forgetfulness."
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	Wind in the neck is located between the sinew of the head and the spine, and therefore it helps with constriction of the chest and breaking up blockages in the pulmonary vein, as well as coughing and fullness.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And therefore it should be released gently, for if it holds too firmly, it can cause harm to the stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	Winds in the two ribs of the neck are beneficial for headaches, ophthalmia, migraines, constriction, and pain in the roots of teeth, and they are located between the sinews of the spine.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And you should command the surgeon to compress his hand on the wound so that he does not cut the artery or cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	Winds under the chin are beneficial for mouth diseases and corruption of gums, as well as similar illnesses that are in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	And it is the place of healing for the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	"Cupping on the shoulders is beneficial for illnesses that come from heat and excess;"
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The dilation of the ribs is worth as much as three veins of the arm, because it attracts blood from those large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the surgeon not to cut too deeply into it, for the place is bare of flesh and has nerves and arteries beneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping glass placed on the buttock is useful for haemorrhoids of the fundament and for diseases below it. It is necessary that the cup be large and made of brass so that it may draw well.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And perhaps if it were thin, it would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	Cupping glasses on the legs heal openly because they attract blood from all over the body, and are useful for old pains in the kidneys, bladder, and hips, and relieve blockages.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	And they are located on the two popliteal spaces and the two ankles, but still they weaken the body after long use and bring about lethargy in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The manner of applying the cupping glass is as follows: first place it empty, and suck temperately, then place it hastily, and move evenly, and do not cease until you see that the spot has turned red and swollen, and the color of blood appears.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then heat, and reset the cups, and take care with the arrangement of the body, for there are those who have thin flesh, and large pores:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	Therefore it is necessary to strike only once, and make wide wounds, a bit deep;
et suce legierement.	and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, then strike twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to refine the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very dense, then strike a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And when we wish to draw blood little by little, one strike suffices.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, then repeat often.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if the blood is thick, strike deep, and the endpoint is that the heart is pierced suddenly. It is necessary for those who have tough and hard skin, and narrow pores, to grease the spots of the cups with clarifying and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is summer, of violet oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of squash seed oil.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it's winter, of cress oil, or of lily, or of chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	"And if the excess blood is thick and cold, use myrrh oil, balsam oil, fennel oil, or similar."
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if one whose skin is tender and has wide pores is treated with a cautery, no oil should be applied there, but it should be washed afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	"And those with excessive moisture should rise using hyssop water, myrtle water, sumac water, or similar substances."
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large excesses rise from old wine, or water of the sieve, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or others similar.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	And they should not use a cupping glass before bathing nor during bathing, but rather after the bath for one or two hours;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And do not sleep after the cupping, and they should warm themselves when they are to be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And warn those who are being bled that if they are choleric and the blood is too thick and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	then they should eat cold things, such as pomegranates and endive and lettuce with vinegar, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And eat pullets, and flesh of castrated animals, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those with cold complexion should take honey syrup and moderately scented wine which is between old and new, and eat little meat and young chickens and small birds.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day he vents himself, he should drink more than he eats.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	It is sometimes necessary to give certain men either treacle or muscat before or after evacuation to strengthen the main members
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	Let the blood be subtly drawn, but it should not be done for those who are hot.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The cupping glasses placed without striking are those placed on the liver, womb, podagra, belly, buttocks, and thighs; for these members do not tolerate being struck upon, and this is only done to draw blood from one member to another, as we place them on the breasts when milk comes out.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	To remove the stiffness from the limb, as we apply cupping glasses to the belly and chest to reduce swelling.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	And relieves pain when there is congestion or stone, its attractive force sometimes draws out the congestion, or dislodges the stone from its position.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	And similarly it does when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind, these cups are applied empty to suck gently only.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	And sometimes they are used together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in diseases of the lungs, so that one fills the cup with warm water or water in which suitable herbs have been cooked.
