Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of administering the cupping glass with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And let there be two cups of half a palm in width and depth, with a small hole on the side around the middle, like that for putting a needle through, made of bronze, softened beforehand so it does not cut the patient when placed on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And let there be in the middle a rod of crosswise earth or iron, to place an enclosed candle upon, and let them be both large and small according to the diseases and the strength of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the cupping glasses for children are different from those for adults, and for thin people they are different from those for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And thus one must place this cupping glass upon the limb
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	light the candle of wax or linen and place it within the cupping glass through the rod that is inside the glass so that the flame is at the bottom of the glass where it will not burn the patient
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it upon the limb so that it is over the opening we spoke of, so that when one wishes, steam can escape and the cupping glass be removed
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and relight the linen as before, and repeat often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	Therefore, in the case of the cupping glass used for pleurisy or any acute disease, there is no rod nor opening, and it is heated only when full of air, and is placed upon the limb alone.
et c’est li forme:	And this is the shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Suction cups are not used except in members where one cannot apply cupping glasses due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And on places without flesh, such as the back or nose, and other similar places;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of using them is that when you find suction cups which are in sharp, clean waters without any defect, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And place one in soft water until they become supple and have nothing inside their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	Then let it be heated with vein and suction cup, then rub the limb until it is red, and place the suction cups on.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are full and hang down, if it is a place where one can apply cupping glasses, then do so, for this is very beneficial.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then lift the place gently and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the wound becomes too hot afterwards on the body of the sick person, then soak a linen cloth in cold water and place it on top until the blood is cooled.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the blood increases, then apply powdered vitriol or salt, and similar things, until it cools down.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or place half a handful of peeled beans on the wound, let them sit until they become warm, and now it will stop bleeding.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more, take additional ones.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the wounds will not close by themselves, then rub fresh blood onto the wound and insert a needle until the blood comes out, then place the beans on top; as soon as they sense the blood, they will become warm.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are full, then sprinkle a little powder made of aloe and sel or ash on them, and now they will burst.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and provides treatment for broken bones and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that foolish physicians throw themselves into this chapter without having seen any of the ancient books or read any letters.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason knowledge is extracted from our land, for I never found any good there.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing of it except through the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the subject, and through experience, and through the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	And I have described for you in this chapter what is contained therein, and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are needed, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	"Therefore, we must say in the prologue of this book the sums of speech and chapters where the wise places his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are tried may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others."
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when any fracture or dislocation or torsion or contusion comes to anyone, you should quickly bandage the patient on both sides if nothing prevents you from doing so, such as weakness of body, or childbirth, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the weather is not quite hot, or too cold
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and avoid cold things, that is to say cold baths, and the flesh of birds and hares, and do not drink wine nor eat any fatty foods, and do not overindulge in meats that fill the veins with blood until you doubt the formation of an abscess or the expansion of matter in the limb.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient returns to their first state of governance which they had used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	"And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the sick person with foods that promote growth and have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, testicles, pears, and veal, eggs, fresh fish, and similar things, and strong wine."
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	"For with this nourishment the wound will close more quickly and completely."
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the elderly and the infirm cannot be well set or joined together according to their nature due to the tenderness of the limbs, nor those which are too soft, such as the bones of young children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but apply a splint to the broken bone with thick bands that will hold it firmly together until it strengthens as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not let any part of its work remain undone, and for this reason, he must be nourished with plenty of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	"And know that breaks are diverse in many ways."
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	"For a break of the head is different from a break of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways that bones can break."
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	"For there are breaks that happen suddenly, and others that occur gradually, such as when cutting a feather to make a writing pen."
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	"And there is also breakage with wounding, and breaking with just a small crack."
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each manner has its own device and proper tool in the restoration process according to what memory brings to mind;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and the breakage of the bone is recognized by the twisting of its place and the gaping opening, and can be felt when pressed with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting nor sound upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no breakage;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it may well have torsion, or fracture, or small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	"So do not move the limb by hand, but apply the medications that come later and then gently immobilize it."
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break which goes up into the shoulder joint, where both parts are dislocated, it is necessary to align them evenly before an abscess forms there.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess forms there, let it be some days until the abscess subsides;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	Then set it back in its place gently and smoothly, knowing that the restoration of this is easier than those with fragments.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then hold it in place, as described below.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken into pieces, then extend both parts, whether it's hand or foot, or hold it with one hand for small limbs, or use two ropes, or one rope and your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And set the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are aligned, gently bring them together using all means, and ensure that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And align the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel with your hand whether it seems well set or not:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If you raise it nicely and do not pull it too tightly or press down as those who cause heat and contractions to the limb through their work, as we have seen many times:
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, instruct the patient not to move it while awake or asleep, turning or in any other manner;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And ensure that the limb is well secured so that no pain is felt.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For if any pain is felt, it is not properly set, and one must position it in such a way that no pain is felt;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And ensure it is placed correctly so that no twisting occurs when it is reset;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For the qualities of a broken limb are as I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	"Know that broken limbs are diverse in size, shape, and thickness."
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	But there are small limbs such as arms and legs and similar ones:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	It is necessary to wrap linen cloths that are soft and fine;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	And those that are thick, like the thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	So one should wrap it with a wide and strong linen bandage, for the wide bandages embrace the entire limb evenly and compress it on all sides without any gap;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then wrap it with light splints, 3 or 4 turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand a little on all the bandage, then go above the fracture and tighten less, so that the fracture may move away from the fracture a little;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And loosen the bandage a little bit at a time until you grasp a large part of the healthy area, then take another bandage and wrap it around again over the fractured area;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the part below the fracture and tighten it moderately, not too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first binding above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the ligaments swabs of linen or cloth pads, as even as possible, then bind all with bandages above, and then place well-made compresses on top, if there is no abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is inflammation or abscess, then place on top something that cools the hot abscess and removes the inflammation, leaving it so for several days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then press upon your compresses with something halfway between a wide reed stalk and a flat piece of wood used for hoes, or palm ribs, and they should be shaped thus:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But the compress placed on the fracture should be somewhat thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And it should also be as long as necessary for the limb's smallness or largeness;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then press upon the compresses as you did on the first binding, then bind above with a linen bandage, just as in the first binding over the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	Narrower above, always less;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	And the thread should be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But if the thread is thick, as I have seen in the work of foolish people who use rope-like threads of linen yarn, this is a great error; for the stitch cannot be even if it is too fine, and there should not be less than two fingers' breadth between each stitch.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is injured by the edges of the stakes after stretching in safe places, then place pads of linen or woolen gauze beneath them so that they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When a wound is accompanied by fracture and the bone is broken, I will describe its treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not advisable to stretch all broken limbs with stakes on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, you should not put any sutures until after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your certainty of a hot abscess occurring;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	And here is the method of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And you should take flour that adheres to the walls of the mill and mix it with plenty of eggs. This mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, should be used for the common method of plastering fractures in many positions, especially for women and small children, as it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of plaster restoring breaks, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take equal amounts of alabaster, ladanum, mullein, asafetida, gum arabic, and myrrh.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloewood, equal parts Z
alechil VIIII З.;	aléchil IX Z
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and grind them into powder, then mix with egg yolk.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the complexion of the man is hot, then use this plaster, for it has good composition and quickly heals broken bones. It benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of plaster that is beneficial for twists:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take myrrh and balsam, equal parts Z
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	myrrh and aloewood, equal amounts Z
acaice VI З.;	acaic VIII Z
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	bolus armoniac X Z, grind well, and combine with honey or egg yolk, then apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another method of plaster for joints and bones dislocated from their places, to alleviate pain, prevent bone wear, and heal fractures:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take new linen, wetting it in both saltwater and cooked oil, then place it upon the wound.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore (set bones), but it is good for soothing a hot boil, and removes pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another method of plaster that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves and terrestrial pennyroyal leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of broken bones and to soften the remainder of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of mistletoe, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour; each one part
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind them together. Then combine with wine and use it if the limb is inflamed; otherwise combine it with moistened coriander water or plain water and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of plaster more powerful than the first one when hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take equal parts of mistletoe root, linseed, balm, melilot, silphium, violet flowers, and chamomile flowers
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind them together. Combine with saltwater or fresh water depending on the inflammation of the limb; otherwise use wine for restful limbs.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not apply anything to the broken limb for setting besides wax and oil ointment, and nothing else more. He also says that it should be of medium consistency, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen believes that one should apply dry and slightly warm things to the broken limb for setting, such as myrrh, aloe, frankincense and similar substances, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another plaster good for injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mullein leaves and chopped male goat hairs, or bird feathers, and almonds, and salt equally, grind them, and make an ointment with the juice.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then, after a few days, check if the patient feels no pain and if the bone has not moved from its place
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	If it does not dislocate again within several days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain or itching appears at the location without rest or swelling, hurry and dislocate again, removing the ointment immediately
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And take a light cloth, a wet sea sponge, dip it in water, and wipe the area until the itching stops and the pain is eased
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply dry linen moistened in water or rose oil, and hold it on with a compress until you are sure there is a warm boil
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and the inflammation of the limb has subsided and the pain is gone, then resume the gentle bandaging, adding a bit of ointment, but not binding it as tightly as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and polish it until it's smooth.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	"And if you see that the abscess is hot and red, and there is pain and swelling, then you must resume binding it with poultice, just as you did initially."
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if no improvement comes to the limb from what we have said, then do not remove the splint until after 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and sometimes leave it on for 20 days, according to what one sees, until the fracture has healed and the flesh approaches union;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then remove the splint more securely, and let the flesh grow thicker, as I said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	And if you see that the place is drying out too much, know that nourishing it cannot happen;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then apply warm water compresses every time you remove the splint, and this should be done every third day, and loosen the bandage a little;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	by this work, nourishment comes quickly to the limb, and it remedies swiftly what foolish physicians do, who restore the limb crookedly:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	That is wicked, and such are cowardly works, and I see nothing else but leave it and work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	"Concerning the different kinds of fractures"
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many types of fractures exist, with diverse shapes, and their causes are distinct.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	For there are fractures caused by the blow of a sword, which breaks all the bone up to the hip joint beneath the bone, like an axe or a tree trunk;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	And therefore this type of fracture is called "hachure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	When the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, this type of fracture is called "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And the wound in these two types of fractures is either large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	"And if there is an embedded fracture, or a break from falling on stones, or from stones falling, or from similar causes."
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	"And if there is an open fracture that approaches the bone marrow, whether it is below or above the bone, this wound is either large or small."
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And there is also a wound that closes up in the bone as fine as a hair, with a small crack, and therefore this fracture is called "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if the wound is made by striking with a stone or falling or something similar, and pushes the bone fragment inward, creating a hollow like that of a cauldron when struck.
si entre li piere dedens.	If stones are present within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this occurs more often among those who have moist bones at their head, such as children's heads.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens in all types of fractures where small fragments are dislodged like stars.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	And I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	"And we recognize all kinds of fractures through direct examination and probing and by the corrupt flesh on top."
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	"The capillary appearance is recognized by this: when the bone is uncovered and rubbed with vinegar, the fracture becomes black."
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	"In treating a fracture, beware of accidents that may occur in illness. If you see no bad accident such as vomiting blood, loss of consciousness, extension and paleness, feverish chill, eyes protruding and turning red, and other similar dispositions in many ways, he cannot be cured without doubt."
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	"And if you see no frightening accident and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment."
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	"And when the injured person first comes to you and it is wintertime, you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the moon that you can."
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	"And if it is in summer, hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day so that the flesh under the bone does not become corrupted and the accidents we mentioned do not occur."
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone extends to the tissue covering the brain, then you must cut open the fractured part as follows:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and that you grasp the patient's head gently and uncover the bone in all possible ways and along the length of the wound as softly as possible; if bleeding occurs during this process or a hot abscess appears, help accordingly, and then fill the space with gauze moistened in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the hot abscess is pacified, and ensure that there is no further bleeding;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to remove around the bone, and this is done in two ways of operation.
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One method is thus: you cut narrowly at the front, and this is its shape.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	"And then I place another chisel larger than the first."
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second manner is thus: have many cuts of diverse widths, some narrow and others wide, pointed, and made of tempered iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work gently, so that you do not wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and strong, you should surround it with holes before administering cuts with tongs, not too deep that they penetrate beyond the soft part of the bone. It must have above its point a margin or circle to prevent the point from passing through the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you should have several such points that each one fits its place on the edge of the bone, so that you have tongs for all uses.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And this is the shape of the three kinds of tongs:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The qualities for piercing around broken bones are that you place the tongs on the bone and turn your hands until you know the bone is pierced.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then move the cautery elsewhere a short time later, and do so all around, then cut with scalpels the space of bone that is between the pores, and do this more finely than you can, and gently, as we have said, until you draw out the bone by hand, or by any tool you have such as forceps.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	And be sure not to touch the brain nor the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and drawn out the bone, then reset the remaining sharpness of the bone with another tool similar to a scalpel, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other scalpels.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if any small bones or scales remain, remove them lightly with one of your tools.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Then dress the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another way of working is what the Gauls say, which is safer;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And tie it very tightly, and this is his command.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	"It is necessary first to uncover part of the bone where the fracture appears more. Then you will place beneath the head of this lenticular chisel, of which this is the shape:"
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut on one side only; the part is sharp on both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Then strike gently with a small hammer all around the bone, and be careful not to injure the tissue beneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is adherent to the bone, scrape it gently, for it can be removed without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	"And if the fracture of the bone does not reach to the skin and the bone is cut only on top with small pieces, then smooth down that roughness and remove the chips with a fine razor, of which you should have many different sizes to use in each place according to the work and the shape of the fracture."
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	"So use larger razors first and then finer ones, continuing until it is all smooth."
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	For each of the other hair cuts and subtle breaks, you must adjust your approach accordingly.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	And this is something that cannot be learned from those who have studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the sinew is exposed, you should take one linen cloth according to the size of the wound, wet it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth doubled over twice or three times, wet it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	And do this more gently than you are able, so as not to injure the surface; then apply the other lien above it, and do not pull too hard, only enough to touch the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	And leave it thus for one or two days until the boil is cooled; then untie it and apply medicines such as lily roots, wheat flour, incense powder, and other similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And grind these substances into a powder, apply it to the wound, and continually apply warm ointments without biting or chewing them.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	And ensure that the wound is always clean, so that no ointment remains or any flies gather on it; for when flies gather on the cloth of the cerecloth, they will corrupt and cause great harm to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	For when corrosive substances are placed on the skin, they necrotize it.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	"So beware, then, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, and be doubtful without doubting too much."
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness appears on the skin due to the medicine applied, which has such power, then take one part honey and three parts rose oil, mix them together in a cloth, and apply it to the skin.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then follows the treatment of various diseases, until he is cured.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes both parts of the nose above are broken, or one part alone, for these are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	And that below is made of cartilage and does not break, but can be bent crooked or twisted, after which it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must put your little finger or thumb into the hole of the nose, and press that break evenly against your index finger, and gently pull from behind, until the nose resumes its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, ensuring that the patient does not feel pain due to your treatment.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	"If the fracture is in the upper part near the elbow and the forearm cannot return to its place, then you must align it with the head of a splint that is somewhat thick."
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if both parts are broken, do the same. And hurry to reset it on the first day if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	But if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling has subsided, then place a bandage made of linen cloth on the tip of the nose if it is broken on one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	If you cut one side off another, then if there is a fracture there.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the openings of the wound.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some doctors say that one must grease the tents with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It seems not good to me that they should be dry, but they must be moistened in a mixture of eggwhite and flour powder.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then leave the bandage until the bone is firm, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes one puts goose feathers in place of bandages, and also wraps it with soft cloth, and if the fracture holds, then the patient breathes more easily.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	do as you see fit
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if gangrene comes nearby while you are working on it, then put cerate or cotton moistened in rose oil, or a little bit of diacalcic on it.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess does not form there, then apply a plaster made from flour of barley and powdered incense mixed with egg white, then place light dressings on top without binding the wound.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the flesh is small, and it is broken into many pieces, then extract with appropriate instruments, then sew the opening, and care for it as things inside the body are cared for, using suitable plasters and ointments.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he has neither a wound nor any other injury inside, treat him with tents and apply splints of lead until he is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Mandible fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken from behind and there is no wound in front, and the break is only on one side without being broken into pieces internally, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	If the fracture is on the right side, you must put your two index fingers into the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is on the left jaw, put your two index fingers of the right hand into the patient's mouth, gently push the fracture in and hold it with your other hand evenly.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone is broken into two pieces and dislocated from each other, then you should apply traction from both sides until it is even again.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if movements of the teeth occur, or dislocations, tie them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk; then apply cerate to the broken jaw and cover it with a double bandage.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And apply a well-made splint or an even piece of leather, long and wide according to the jawbone, and tie it securely. Command the patient to rest and eat soft foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the alignment has changed, untie it on the third day and then carefully reposition what was dislocated;
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	And place emplastrum on top, of flour ground with abundance of eggs or sesame flour, after what you have removed the cerote.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	And place a light linen bandage on top, and if the emplastrum dries out, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it is healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Healed many times in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if inflammation comes with heat, then apply what we have said many times [i.e., treat the inflammation as previously described].
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is fracture and wound together, examine if no piece of the bone is broken off;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if with suitable tools you can extract it.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with fire according to your necessity [i.e., cauterize it].
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all the broken pieces and none remain, then sew up the wound if it is large, and place over it one of the poultices suitable for promoting granulation until it is healed.
de la forcele	Here is an entry from a medieval French medical manuscript about reducing fractures of the jawbone (mandible):
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The shoulder blade has broken many times before, and the fracture is of three kinds:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	either it is broken but not dislocated in two places with pieces, which is easiest to reset;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or there is fracture with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the procedure when the fracture is without wound is that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder blade which feels the broken bone;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	And the other extends the neck towards the part.
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Then place the break evenly on your two teeth so that the shape is as it should be, with neither appearance nor displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend further, place a round pad of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder according to your necessity;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And stretch and lift the wrist gently, pressing the pad with your hand so that you place the break evenly as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you are unable to grasp the head of the forceps at the front because it is too deep, then the patient should lie on their back with their shoulders supported by a pillow. Insert a medium-sized ear spoon under the shoulder, and have an assistant press down on the shoulder until the bone of the forceps lifts up.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	Then align the break with your teeth, and if you find it unstable, you must cut into it;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and gently pull apart the pieces. If the bone cannot join due to any obstruction, then cut one of the incisions that you have;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	But place this tool under the wrist to guard against dislocation:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	And it should resemble a spoon, not be raised, and be as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and the power of the work;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And let there be two heads [of the cautery], as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, like the route of the wound that you made when you treated the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure that the abscess is hot, cut the wound, and if the route is small or you doubt the heat of the abscess, fill the wound with rags and compresses according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot inflammation occurs, then soak one cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The bandaging of the bone when there are no wounds and no cuts is that you place on the bone the poultice made from flour and oak bark, and put light dressings on top, and place a splint under the limb if necessary;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very wide bandage about a palm's width in length, then place two cloths on top of the dressings and poultice;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a thin strip of linen about three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang loose;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And place the needle on the break, and wrap the bandage above the neck, and below the healthy shoulder, and below the dislocated shoulder.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And then reset each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the break well, and you clearly see that the needle does not move from the broken bone, then reinforce it every day. And once the ligature loosens, restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	And make the patient lie on his back and put a small pillow under the shoulder when he sleeps to lift up the shoulder.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	Thus lighten the break's pressure by lifting the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck and do not untie it in case of an accident for up to 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then recommence the reduction if necessary, and hold it and leave it thus until it is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And it is restored within 28 days, but for some men less time passes.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Here ends the treatment for a broken shoulder.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It happens that the shoulder joint breaks or moves out of place, and one cannot know unless touched.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	If it appears according to the shape of the break, and you reset it according to its natural form in all ways possible.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then place on the joint powder from a millstone with abundant egg whites, and light bandages, and cover with a doubled cloth.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then place over it a wide and thin splint, slightly larger than the shoulder, and if there are any hairs under the splint in some part of the shoulder, wrap those hairs with linen bandages so that the splint lies evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then bind it tightly with a large bandage so that the splint does not move from its place, and check the binding each day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time he moves, bind it tightly, and keep the splint even if it has moved from its place, and have the patient lie on his side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	And the shoulder is reset in twenty days or twenty-five.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is completed, then remove it, and be sure of it, for it is not bone that can set itself easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone sticks out and is not under the heart, then cut it off, and do what we have said in the treatment for a broken collarbone to calm the hot inflammation.
de la brisure dou pis	Here ends the treatment for a broken shoulder blade
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The leg sometimes breaks in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	But it often breaks at the lower end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it breaks in mid-air, it leans downwards and the patient feels great pain, faints quickly, often vomits blood, and sometimes the bone marrow is visible through the broken bone.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and puts a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders together, and brings the ribs of the two sides close with your hands, carefully bringing them even in all ways you can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then places plasters and bandages above the subtle layer of salt or another light wood, wrapped in a cloth, and holds it on the broken bone so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and ties the bandage evenly around the back, and tightens it moderately, and releases each hour a little, and if it loosens, then tightens it;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	And if it needs to be untied, due to corrosion or itching that occurs there, or pain or abscess, then hasten and untie it, and remove the emplaster, and apply remedies suitable for the situation.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then reset the emplaster, and hold it firmly until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	"of the breaking of the ribs"
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that fractures of the ribs occur only in large areas after the back and at the head within, and they break only because they are smooth.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	And one can feel it well upon examination, as you will see.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment for this is to set the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply a splint, and secure it with a bandage if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the fracture of the ribs is inward, the patient feels great pain and piercing, like a stitch in the side, because the bone pierces the flesh.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And it leads to paleness and fainting, and vomiting of much blood, and this indicates serious illness, and those who are experienced have put great effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	"And there are those who say that it should be administered foods that swell the belly, to push the break outwards."
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	"We do not do this, lest many boils come if they were not there before."
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	"And if they have come, then heal them."
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And some say that one should apply cupping glasses to the area to suck strongly, which seems reasonable.
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	Despite this, there is doubt that the cupping glasses will draw out the excesses to their proper place due to weakness of disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	"And some say that one should cover the spot with damp wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to keep the bandage even around it, then treat with the pleurisy remedy of meat and medicine."
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	If the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear due to the bone pressing on the skin, and there is doubt about this, then one must cut upon the site of the broken rib, and place a tool underneath to support the side.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then one must saw through the bone, gently pull it out, and afterwards sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, cleaning it with poultices until it is clean.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if a swelling comes out in the form of an abscess, then place moistened cloths dipped in rose oil on top, and apply them to the site.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat the site as if it were an abscess until it is healed, keeping it warm on that side constantly until it is clean.
de la brisure dou col	"concerning the fracture of the neck"
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes there is a break in the bones of the neck, and it happens that they bend;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	And also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will heal or not, take note if you see their hands softened, swollen, and lifeless, and cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many cases, and if he moves them and feels when they are pressed or pricked, know that the bone joints are saved, and that the patient will be cured if treated.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if such thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know whether it is healthy or not, then observe if the feet are softened, and if there are accidents in the hands, and on the back windiness and involuntary expulsion occur;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And when they fall asleep on their belly, involuntary expulsion occurs.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is asleep on his back and wants to mount, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is mortal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	If one does not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not occur, then the case is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that you apply if there is a hot abscess; put rose oil or oil of rue on the spine until it is appeased;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then place one of the comforting and drying emplasters, and the glue of a linden tree, and instruct the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And do not let them sleep on that part where they feel pain until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone separates, then cover the chest;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And remove the bone, then join together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with one suture, then heal it with ointment surrounding the flesh until it is clean.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	And if the bone head is broken, which is called the 'cow's head', insert your left hand's pouch and place it even with the other hand at full power, then put the splint and bandage on top if needed.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then bind it, and if there is displaced bone, cut and remove it, and heal the wound until it is clean.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Regarding the fracture of the thighbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	If the thighbone is broken, there will be a slight loss of function at the top;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	And cut it along its length, declining towards the divided end, and it brings the patient pain and throbbing where it is broken, with swelling around it.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And to set it right, stretch your hand upwards until you are above the break;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	And know what is the breakage and the shape of it;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	If the break is at the head only, then set that break even with its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	"And if the fracture is long or slants inward, then make the patient lie on their stomach so that the reduction of that fracture may be convenient."
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it even, then place a splint, then place a wooden or bone rod on top of it and hold the break so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and tie the sling under the armpit until the sling is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	"And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back."
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if a red abscess comes up there, do not touch it until the red abscess has abated, and then place what we have mentioned before;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to setting it right, and hold it as it should be held if there is no bad complication;
et c’est li maniere.	And that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder blade is what is between the chest and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one should reset it according to one of these two ways:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	Of which one is that you take a piece of large-grained wheaten flour, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie two lengths of linen around the head, and hang them upwards, and have the patient sit on a seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then cast his broken arm onto the board until it reaches the elbow and is in the middle of its curve, then hang some heavy weight on it or have the assistant hold it down;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then align the break with his hands together, so that the break returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another method is to prop up the patient on their bed and have them hold their hand at their neck; then command two ministers such that one pulls the part above the break towards him while the other pulls the lower part downwards, each one stretching in his respective direction.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction should be stronger, then hold the ligature below the fracture and above it, and extend each of the assistants to their respective places.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the break is near the head of the shoulder, then you must place one length of linen underneath the elbow and another towards the side, underneath the break;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and similarly if the break is towards the side, one length of linen should be placed lightly and without force so that the break is aligned with its proper position on the side;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	then align the break properly and bind it firmly, lest any swelling occur.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess appears, do not incise it until seven days have passed; instead, apply moistened linen with rose oil, until the abscess subsides.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then incise it, and the method of incision is to place the spatula on the break, then bring the arm up towards the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And then bind it with bandages, holding the shoulder and arm in place so that the arm is in its proper position unless something prevents it or if the bone has moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone may move, use splints; place a broader and stronger splint on the break, with two fingers' space between each splint, ensuring each splint is wide enough to extend three fingers beyond either side of the break.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then bind around the splints, as I mentioned at the beginning of this chapter concerning fractures, binding more tightly and without stretching.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the swelling of the joints, and the tension, as we have mentioned, in the place where you reset the broken limb, and you suspect a hot abscess, leave it alone until the seventh day, as we have said.
